That made her focus on Bruce’s current strength again.

He could definitely squash any average adventurer out there. Merely being able to be admitted into the tower meant he was one of the best spellcasters out there.

But in this tournament, things were more complicated. Everyone across the continent had heard about it, attracting various adventurers with power far above the average.

「By the way, Bruce. How strong are the sisters you formed a Contract with yesterday?」

Mira decided to ask about that. Valkyries were some of the strongest summons one could obtain, and could serve as Bruce’s trump card if needed. But before that, they needed to know just how strong they were in their current state.

Back when Mira first formed a Contract with Alfina and her sisters, they were mediocre at best when compared to the other Valkyries. They were still far stronger than the average human warrior, but not enough to really compete in a big tournament like that.

After many battles alongside Danbulf, gaining plenty of combat experience, they matured into the strongest Valkyries in Valhalla.

Meanwhile, only one day had passed since Bruce formed his Contract with Valkyries, so they had no experience yet. So Mira wanted to know how strong they were currently, and if they would be of help in the tournament or not.

「How strong? Well…obviously they’re not as strong as Alfina, but they really surprised me. My Dark Knight stood no chance against them.」

He said that with a hint of pride. But Mira mumbled, 「That really doesn’t serve as much of a comparison for me,」 and decided to go straight to the source instead, telling Bruce to summon them so Mira could test them herself.

「Right away!」

Mira had implicitly told him that she doubted his strength, but that did not make him upset or combative. After all, it was one of the Nine Wisemen telling him that, and if anyone had the knowledge and experience to claim that, it was her. So Bruce did as told and summoned his Valkyries without a second thought.

(Oh… He’s quite adept at this.)

He started by forming a Binding Arcana Circle, which he transmuted into a Rosario Summoning Circle. Those were necessary steps for a high level summoning, so it was important being able to conduct them rapidly. Everything from the formation of the spells, chanting, and construction of the summoning gate was performed flawlessly by Bruce.

「We three sisters are here at your service.」

The Valkyrie Helcune stepped out of the summoning circle, followed by Erne, and Lagrinne. Bruce stared at them stunned, before his eyes filled with emotion.

「Ah… I still can’t believe I’ve done it…」

He was still trying to process that he had already formed a Contract with the Valkyries, and that his first time summoning them had worked without a hitch, and when it sunk in, he looked to the sky, like he could pass away with no regrets now.

While Bruce remained in that state, the three sisters also began to show a strange reaction.

「Wait, is this…」  

「But how…」  

「There, are they…」

There were only clouds in the skies above, a building like a palace stood a distance away, and on the opposite side were seven Valkyries training. The moment the three noticed that, they stiffened up in shock, realizing they were on the highest island of Valhalla.

Almost instinctively, the three trotted up to hide behind Bruce, trying to not be seen by the seven, and whispered 「Jude, what exactly do you need from us?!」

「Hm? Ah, right, sorry. There’s something Mira wanted to ask from you.」

Bruce finally snapped back and replied to them, and then pointed behind where they stood. The three sisters followed his finger, finally spotting Mira there, before frantically taking formation and kneeling down.

「Sovereign! Our deepest apologies for not greeting you sooner.」

The three of them kept their heads low, and Mira just waved it away with a bit of laughter, saying she did not mind. Mira felt like they always fussed about her position too much, but she knew that if she told them to take things more lightly, they would politely refuse, adhering to their code of conduct. So Mira just tried to move on, bringing up the reason why she had asked to see them.

Mira wanted to know how strong they were, and the sisters answered by detailing which Valkyries they had defeated, and which they had lost to, essentially a useless reply for anyone who did not live there.

There were no monsters in Valhalla either, being a space mainly inhabited by Valkyries, so there was very little that could be used as comparison there.

Mira then thought of bringing Alfina and her sisters for a practice match, but Helcune and her sisters said they were so far behind the seven that they would be beaten instantly, yet again providing no real comparison.

In the end, Mira decided to use a more direct approach and summoned her Dark Knights. It would take some time, but as she was extremely familiar with the capabilities of her Dark Knights, it would give her the most accurate information.

「Hmm, I think I’ve got it now.」

Some ten odd minutes later, Helcune and her sisters were done proving each of their capabilities against a seemingly endless wave of Dark Knights. The last one to fall exhausted was Erne, signaling the end of Mira’s test.

The three had roughly the same amount of power, being more or less on par with someone like Sasori, a member of the Fifty Bells’ elite Hidden group.

In adventurer terms, she would fall right in the middle of rank A. Strong enough in most cases, but there would be many stronger opponents in the tournament. It was easy to imagine that the finalists of the tournament would be far above rank A anyway, so Bruce needed something better if he wanted to get that far.

「Okay, I know what to do.」

After some quick thinking, Mira decided on the best way to improve their abilities. She turned around and waved while shouting loudly 「Heyyy, Alfinaa!! Come here for a minute!」

She was calling in the direction of the seven sisters, who were currently practicing a 3v3v1 fight. They were ferocious, the clashing of their various weapons clearly audible even from far away. Obviously enough, the one fighting on her own was Alfina.

Even when outnumbered like that and having to focus to maintain her ground, she was the first one to react to Mira’s call. As soon as she spotted Mira waving, she zoomed over almost like she was dashing through the air.

「What do you need, Master.」

Alfina had run like an approaching tidal wave, but as soon as she was in front of Mira, she knelt in the most refined way possible. Helcune and her sisters watched in amazement, before quickly getting nervous.

「Actually, it’s not about me, but those three there.」

Saying that, Mira glanced over to the three sisters hiding behind Bruce. Alfina followed Mira’s gaze and commented, 「They put up a good fight, didn’t they?」

Even while far away, she had seen the three fighting against Mira’s Dark Knights, but her voice rang slightly harsh, almost like she was jealous that they had gotten to practice directly with her Master.

The three did not pick up on that, and were just happy to be praised by Alfina.

「Now Alfina, I want to ask a favor from you, and as I mentioned, it’s about those three. Would you mind letting them train alongside you for a while?」

Mira asked Alfina to be in charge of training the three sisters, while also explaining the reason why. Summoners were still largely looked down on, and having Valkyries perform well in the tournament would have a big impact in changing that perception.

Alfina’s training regiment placed a lot of emphasis on the fundamentals of combat, and was proven to bring success in actual battle.

Christina’s cries told Mira how ruthless and strenuous it was too, but there was no better approach to prepare for a tournament in such a short time than that.

「We’ll be training as spellcasters here as well, so I’d appreciate it if you could bring them to a higher level on your side.」

The three sisters were still catching up on what was happening, but Mira just went ahead asking again 「So, can I count on you?」 and Alfina instantly replied affirmatively.

「I’ll do anything you wish, Master! I vow on my life that I’ll follow your desires, and thoroughly train them for as long as you need!」

There was no bigger honor for Alfina than to receive such a direct request from Mira, so her heart set ablaze, she raised her sword and announced her determination to fulfill it.

+++

# 307: Training Days

A few hours passed since Helcune and her sisters joined Alfina and the rest to train. They also went over the basics at first, before starting a 3v3v3v1 practice battle. Overall, they seemed to be having a hard time adjusting, as their cries could be heard from afar pretty often.

「Are you sure they’re going to be alright..?」

Bruce turned in the direction of those cries, looking concerned, and Mira just grinned, saying, 「If you can still worry about others then we aren’t training hard enough,」 and summoned another wave of Dark Knights.

That made all color drain from Bruce’s face.

Mira was currently training Bruce to be more adept at evading attacks from enemies, while bringing forth high level summons at the same time.

His partial summoning was still a bit clumsy, but he was able to make shields appear to block the Dark Knight’s relentless attacks and continue chanting.

Despite it all, Bruce continued to prove his strength, succeeding in completing the spells many times. Still, that was only the beginning of his hardships.

The Dark Knights were equipped with wooden training swords instead of their usual black blades. The White Serpent Asclepius was also wrapped around Mira’s arm, ready to heal Bruce at any moment. They were taking a really spartan approach to training, as unlike Helcune and her sisters, Mira and Bruce only had a week to train there.

There were also theory study sessions waiting for Bruce later, as Mira would drill him on more knowledge involving summoner abilities.

When Bruce would later recount those moments, he described them as the most strenuous, but also the most fruitful week of his life.

Time seemed to fly by like that, and before they realized, it was time for dinner. Everyone sat down and ate merrily. Helcune and her sisters were also eating with them, as Alfina had told them to live in the palace until she determined that they had improved to an acceptable level.

Earlier in the day when they heard that, the three were excited to set foot in the palace, but that excitement was gone now.

The exhaustion from training all day was weighing heavily on them, as they lay sprawled on the table, their eyes fatigued and struggling to stay open.

The seven sisters also looked tired, but not to the extent of Helcune and the other two. It was clear that the last stretch of training had been really physically demanding.

Frodina was not as exhausted, as she had ended early to prepare dinner.

Then there was Christina, who looked like she was about to pass away during training, but had swung back to life shortly after it ended. Or rather, she was the most energetic precisely because training was over.

「Master, Master, apparently we’ll get dessert with dinner too!」

Christina said that with a bright smile, still celebrating that Mira had arranged for them to be able to eat sweets again. She then began, 「Also, could you—」 only to cut herself off, quickly adding, 「I’ll tell you another time!」 before dashing off to her seat.

A moment later, Alfina entered the dining hall. She had just finished compiling all the information on the three sisters’ current state and strength, as well as their training plan moving forward. All of that was written down in a chart, which Alfina presented to Mira.

「Hmm, I see. This looks pretty well balanced.」

Alfina’s discerning eye had clearly noticed the traits of the three sisters, and had already come up with the best plan to suit them.

Helcune was most proficient with a shield and would be placed in a defensive position, Erne was a close range fighter, and Lagrinne was best suited at medium range.

「What do you think, Bruce? This is the formation I found most suitable to their abilities, but maybe it could use some adjustments depending on your own abilities and strategies.」

After reporting to Mira, Alfina went to the next seat where Bruce was, to hear what he thought as well. After all, it was the summoner who would direct the formation in the end.

「No, this is flawless. Please proceed like this.」

Bruce did not have any close range combat abilities like Mira’s Sage Arts, so two frontliners and a middle guard was perfect to keep him in the backline.

「Leave it to me.」

Alfina bowed respectfully before heading to where the three sisters were sitting, tapping on their exhausted shoulders and showing them the training plan.

Helcune tried to scream, but her voice was completely gone.

---

「Oh, Sound Visualization. That sounds useful…there, written down.」

After a bustling dinner time, Mira went to her room to wind down, reading the Encyclopedia of Skills in search for anything that could be of use. Then, just like the day before, someone came to visit her room.

「…Okay, the coast is clear.」

Her head poked into the room, and after checking for any other visitors, Christina ran inside in tears saying, 「Master, please do somethingggg!」

「Hmm, I seem to remember you also said something like that last night. What is it?」

That time, Alfina had been in the room as well, so Christina had turned around to run away as soon as she entered. This time, they were alone, so Mira could glean that Christina did not want Alfina to hear whatever she would say.

When Mira asked about it, unsurprisingly, Christina began to complain and beg about training.

「…And usually that would be it for training, but now…」

As she explained, after their already strenuous training, Alfina suddenly decided to start one-on-one matches against herself, easily beating everyone.

Their training already involved fighting in groups of three against Alfina alone, showing just how strong she was. And then she still had the energy to fight everyone else one-on-one at the end and emerged victorious, showing why she was considered the strongest in Valhalla.

But Christina also mentioned that they had never done that before, this was the first time.

「I feel like she’s going over the top just because you’re here. So she’s going to keep doing that tomorrow, and the day after, and so on…So please! Could you at least come to check up on us?! Or maybe…」

Christina desperately pleaded, wanting to avoid going through that again. But was soon interrupted as someone knocked on the door. She instantly twitched, looking at the door in terror as her trembling voice said, 「It can’t be…」

Mira loudly said, 「Come in,」 and surely enough, the new visitor was none other than Alfina.

「Master, I’d like to continue where I left off last night. May I borrow the Holy Sword again?」

Alfina wanted to continue practicing a special move with the Holy Sword Sanctia. She was also looking forward to being granted the honor of holding that sword by her master again, as her eyes twinkled with expectation.

「Sure, go ahead. But only until midnight at most. You’ll rest properly when it gets too late, got it?」

Knowing Alfina, she was capable of staying up all night practicing, so Mira made sure to be stern about it. Mira’s assumption was completely right, as Alfina said, 「As you wish,」 with a slightly disappointed voice.

But her mood swung back as soon as the Holy Sword Sanctia was summoned, and she knelt down to accept it, trembling with excitement.

「Ahh, this is such an honor!」

She exclaimed with elation as she stood up and turned around, ready to leave, something Christina was really hoping for, but contrary to her wishes, Alfina’s eyes landed right on her.

「By the way, Christina, is something wrong with our training? I believe I heard something about checking on it.」  

「Huh?! Umm, I mean…that’s…」

It seemed Alfina had overheard their previous conversation, but only the last part.

Christina was panicking internally, trying to figure a way out of this. After a short time, she thought of something and continued speaking.

「I was just thinking… It’s been a long time since the last time we switched up our training regiment. A lot of things have changed since then, there’s that Holy Sword now…or those Ashen Knights… Our Master has also changed in many ways…」

Already used to coming up with excuses, there was no stopping Christina once she started, so she continued building up on that.

They had been training the same way for more than thirty years now, and now Christina was putting into question whether that was still the ideal way to continue for themselves and their master.

If the tools available to them and their strategies had evolved, then it made sense for their training to evolve as well. Especially considering that Mira had also grown stronger since back then, and had many new attack strategies at her disposal.

Christina continued bringing up points like that one after another, eventually bringing up her own solution to all that..

「That’s why I thought that. It’d be nice if she could come check on our training sometime, so she can point out what we should work on more, what isn’t needed anymore, or if we’re going overboard with something, or maybe something doesn’t make sense to do… I just want her to point us in the correct direction!」

Christina said all that while looking straight into Alfina’s eyes, acting like those were all her honest feelings and there was nothing to hide. But in reality, there was not a smidge of truth to it.

(It’s almost impressive that she can keep on talking for so long without tripping on her own words…)

She was not just used to lying and coming up with excuses, but seemed to almost have a divine talent for it. It was like she was a natural born charlatan. Mira was astonished to witness that, but she also enjoyed the show, and remained silent to see how Alfina would react.

「It’s rare to see you of all people taking training so seriously.」

Alfina felt like something was up, staring at Christina trying to figure out what was happening. Her gaze was piercing, discerning what was true or not, and an ordinary person would feel forced to confess all crimes when subjected to that.

But Christina was already used to that stare, and calmly looked back at Alfina, acting like everything she had just said was really the reason why she was there.

Or rather, it was like she had made herself believe all of that while she was saying it. Especially the last part, her true desires were concealed there, as she wanted to be free from what she felt were needless parts of training.

It had all started with lies, but ended up honest claims, making Christina confident in her excuse. Christina’s eyes remained unwavering, compelling Alfina to mull over everything she said and reach the conclusion that there was some merit to it.

「I see, you might have a point there.」

Alfina began nodding to herself, beginning to question whether their current training regiment really was the best they had. She was not just thinking it over, but almost seemed to be looking forward to enacting Christina’s suggestion.

After all, it would mean that not only would Mira watch them, they would receive direction from her, something Alfina had only dreamt of before.

「What do you think, Master? My sister usually never thinks about training this seriously, so could you do it for her too?」

Alfina’s neverending reverence for Mira made her hesitant to make such big requests, but as Christina was the one who had brought it up, she stood in support of her sister.

「Hmm, that’s a good idea. It’d also help for me to know in more detail what you’re doing.」

After a short pause, Mira agreed to go watch them train the next day.

Things had taken a confusing turn, with Alfina and Christina’s expectations standing at odds but somehow becoming aligned in the end. At the same time, Mira felt like that would be the perfect opportunity for her to test out new battle formations and tactics she had thought up.

「Thank you very much, Master!」

Christina thanked her profusely, implicitly saying, 「please make things easier for me too.」

「I can’t thank you enough.」

Alfina was also overjoyed by it, but kept her emotions in check while bowing politely.

And so, it was decided that Mira would watch and inspect their training the next day. With everything discussed, Alfina turned around and left with a brisk gait, almost like she had grown angel wings out of delight, being granted the honor of holding the Holy Sword and knowing that Mira would direct them personally the next day. Christina also left, at an even faster pace, as she wanted to get as far away as possible before Alfina started to suspect anything.

(Now, what should I do about Bruce’s training… Hmm, maybe I can accelerate the pace a bit, as he’s an excellent student.)

Mira closed the Encyclopedia of Skills and brought out her notepad, reading through the ideas she had written down so far, already excited about trying them out the next day.

---

The next morning welcomed their third day in Valhalla.

After breakfast, it was time to start training, and Mira went to the bigger training area together with Alfina, her sisters, as well as Helcune and her sisters.

「…By Christina’s request, our Master is here today to inspect our training regiment. Look alive everyone!」

The Valkyries gathered there all gave a loud positive reply in unison, almost like the rallying cheer of a sports event.

(Hmm…at least it seems they like the idea.)

Mira was relieved to see that all of the Valkyries there were into the idea. She knew how fastidious it could be to deal with a meddling boss during work, but the Valkyries did not see her that way, and instead welcomed her there.

Then, Alfina began detailing what they would focus on that day, while glancing over to Christina from time to time, who was pretending to be paying attention, when really she kept looking at Mira whenever Alfina’s eyes weren’t on her.

Christina’s eyes seemed to constantly be repeating, 「Don’t forget what I told you.」

All Christina wanted was for the hellish training to become softer, and Mira was the only person in the world who could accomplish that.

(Somehow. I feel like it’s not just her who wants that…)

Mira soon realized that all six younger sisters were glancing at Mira with pleading eyes from time to time, showing just how harsh their training had been thus far, and she decided to keep that in mind when watching what they would do.

And as far as Bruce was concerned, Mira’s actual student at the moment…he was a distance away, being chased by an Ashen Knight.

After telling him that she would be watching the Valkyries train, Mira left him some homework so he could keep himself busy.

His task was to defeat an Ashen Knight using only partial summoning. Only a few days had passed since he had learned that ability, and this was his first time putting it to work in a fight.

So far, he had proven adept at summoning a shield, but he had not quite gotten the knack of swords yet. That was a step he needed to overcome if he wanted to defeat the Ashen Knight.

The Ashen Knights were equipped with wooden swords for training, but getting hit was still painful. Any actual injuries were instantly healed by Asclepius, so although there was no danger, there was no avoiding the pain.

His success rate was still low when attacking, but he would have to keep trying if he wanted to complete the task. He had no choice but to stop running and defending as much, and allot some of his mana to fight back. He was like a courageous lion cub enduring an enormous trial.

(This is even crazier than I expected…)

Around two hours later, their warmup exercise of swinging a weapon thirty thousand times was over. Mira had initially imagined practice swings like those conducted in kendo or baseball batting, but Valkyries did something slightly different.

It was almost surreal how they swung their swords multiple times a second, the sound of the air being cut resembling a storm.

That was something Alfina made them do every single day to begin their training. But it was the number of swings that really seemed excessive, and left them exhausted from the get go.

Helcune and her sisters, the newcomers, had already fallen within the first hour.

Alfina showed some leniency for them, understanding that they were just starting to adjust. But that was still Alfina, so after ten minutes of rest, she forced them to resume.

(This really feels way too extreme…)

There was a fifteen minute break before they moved onto their next training exercise. Christina and her sisters already looked dead, their eyes begging Mira, letting her know that this was the first thing they wanted her to amend.

Only Alfina stood tall and proud, having not broken a sweat yet, truly showing that it had been a warmup exercise for her.

Alfina had always been ahead of the rest of the sisters in strength, and that gap was more evident than ever now.

(At first, I thought it was just Christina’s usual whining, but some reform is definitely needed here.)

Gaining a new outlook on the matter, Mira opened her notebook and began jotting down what stood out the most to her. The younger sisters noticed that, bringing a hint of hope back to their lifeless eyes.

+++

# 308: New army

A few hours passed with Mira watching Alfina and her sisters train, until they were done for the day. Mira’s first impression was basically an ample amount of relating to Christina’s feelings.

“It was really helpful to take the time to watch just how much effort you’re all putting into training.”

The dining hall had been turned into a debriefing meeting to discuss their performance that day.

Helcune and her sisters were there too, continuing the training they began the day before, but they were so exhausted that they just lay sprawled against the table. Bruce was in similar shape to them, his pale face reminiscent of the color of the Ashen Knights he had been pitted against.

Mira began the meeting by praising the seven sister’s efforts, and Alfina showed the biggest reaction to that. “Your words are too kind,” she replied, trembling with emotion. The younger sisters also looked happy, but they did not show it as much as they were really looking forward to what Mira would mention next.

“Now then…the main thing that stuck out to me was…”

She explained how overall she had a positive impression, but that she felt it was a bit too hard, especially when it came to how many repetitions they did. It made sense for things like practice swings, but in their case, they included things like charging into attack, and more complex moves, repeated a ridiculous number of times.

Mira brought that up and told Alfina to amend that, pointing out that there was a limit to how much one’s body could take, and that proper time to rest and recover was also important to train optimally.

Not to mention that, Alfina was quite far ahead compared to her sisters, so even if she could handle that punishing training, it was far too much for the rest and there was no need for them to match her.

“Is that so…?!”

Alfina’s eyes widened with fright hearing that, as she had been mindlessly pushing her sisters forward so they would improve, but she listened to Mira and checked their schedule again, and noticed what Mira was referring to.

That produced a collective sigh of relief from Christina and the rest, as Alfina finally understood their plight. At the same time, they celebrated their master’s benevolence.

But the conversation was not over yet.

“If we trim down the excess, you’ll end up with a lot more free time, right? So I was thinking…”

That was actually Mira’s main goal, freeing up the Valkyries’ time to put it into something more worthwhile for her. So she made a few suggestions.

Her main goal was to assemble new lineups for small platoons and armies, which would utilize the power of Armor Spirits she had recently expanded upon through her research and experiments in the Tower.

The Valkyrie Sisters would be commanding those armies, necessitating their familiarity with those new powers. Finding the way to accomplish that was another of the reasons why Mira had agreed to watch them train.

“To start off, take a look at this.”

Mira glanced at all of them as she said that and promptly summoned three of her staple Dark Knights. But they did not look the same as usual.

They were not carrying their black swords.

Instead, one had a pike, another a battleaxe, and the last a bow. That was the heart of her research, getting Armor Spirits to fight with new weapons.

They had shown new aptitude to learn, including the ability to extract figments of power from other spirits wielding weapons different from swords. Having discovered that, she headed straight to an Ancient Battlefield in search for more Armor Spirits. In the end, she obtained those three types.

“I see what you mean…”

Different weapons also meant different fighting styles, so it was better to think of them as completely new Dark Knights. Alfina was surprised to see that, but she quickly caught onto what Mira was trying to say.

Battleaxes had more destructive power than swords, making them better to weaken an opponent’s defences. Just holding a pike created a deterrent, boasting with far greater reach than a sword as well. And the bow’s advantages were obvious enough.

Being able to position and command such Dark Knights would allow Mira’s army to be far more versatile than ever before.

Currently, that was all merely a possibility. Alfina and her sisters needed to become familiar with them and practice to make it a reality in armies with more than a thousand troops.

So Mira handed them a certain book, wanting them to learn how to use the brand new Dark Knights.

“That’s why I asked Solomon to get me this recently.”

That book was a collection of battle tactics and training, carefully compiled to teach how to manage soldiers.

The ones who had gathered all that information were Reynard, Commander of the Imperial Knight Guards; Joachim, Solomon’s trusted confidant; most of the generals from various divisions of Arkite’s army; and even Instructor Arlon. All of them had been personally appointed to the task by Solomon.

Mira had received it without much thought, but that book contained all the information regarding Arkite’s army, how it trained, operated, their secret tactics, and all sorts of other knowledge.

“Let me see…interesting…! This is marvelous!”

Alfina took and briefly leafed through it, quickly realizing the value of the content within its pages. She was already looking forward to seeing what else was written there, but had to stop to continue the conversation.

Her eyes were filled with excitement, convinced that the day they mastered all the knowledge of the book, they would be able to command the most powerful army in the world.

“So, what do you think? Do you want to give it a try?”

So far, Mira was only doing that as a suggestion, so now she wanted to see how they would react.

“I’ll do my best!”

Christina replied right away. Partly because it was an idea coming from their master, but mostly because she dreaded whatever accursed training regiment Alfina would come up with next if nothing else filled the time they had freed up.

And at least, Mira’s suggestion did not require much physical effort.

“I guess this means I’ll be leading the archers then.”

Eletina was also in agreement, followed by the rest of the sisters. And surprisingly enough, all of them seemed interested in it, even if it meant a new type of training, and none seemed displeased by the idea.

If anything, the relentless training they had undergone so far had fortified their tolerance for training, so they felt like they would barely notice their new studies.

Since that was the final day of the hellish schedule, and they were going to start doing something different soon, they were all excited about it and kept talking about it during dinner.

That conversation carried on past dinner, turning into a bit of a meeting to discuss exactly how they would tackle it.

“This came…from King Solomon..? I can hardly picture that…”

While the sisters were engrossed in planning out their schedule, dinner had revived Bruce, who now looked through the book in astonishment.

There were plenty of books discussing military tactics out in the world, but he noticed that there was one big distinction separating this one from the rest.

“I was taught military strategy growing up, but I’ve never seen such extreme methods before.”

He had grown up as the son of a noble family, his father working for the army as well, giving Bruce plenty of contact with such books which made that difference glaringly obvious to him.

The tactics contained within the book Solomon had created with the aid of the highest ranking officers of Arkite had no compassion for casualties.

All the tactics within were purely focused on achieving their goal, regardless of the sacrifices necessary. They were bloody, harsh, almost inhumane in their pursuit of victory.

If future historians found that book, they would paint King Solomon as a cruel tyrant, with a heart of stone and no tears to shed. That was how relentless those tactics were.

Just a cursory glance at the book made Bruce shudder.

It was clear that the book had been written for Mira’s eyes only.

No general would ever subject his soldiers to such tactics in actual war. Unless they happened to command an army that could remain standing with no losses no matter how much damage they took.

An army only someone like Mira could build up with Armor Spirits.

The whole book had been written with that premise in mind.

If they succeeded, Arkite would gain a nearly impenetrable bulwark. And that was something Bruce mentioned aloud.

“Oh… I didn’t realize it went that far.”

Mira had casually asked for it, and just as casually received it. She just thought it was a basic primer on the art of war. Something she could use to get her new army rolling.

But now, she realized it was something that went much, much deeper than just that, thanks to Bruce’s reaction to it.

With a newfound sense of gratitude to Solomon, she rejoined the seven sisters, who were still discussing who would be in charge of what troops. Behind them, Bruce and Helcune’s sisters also began to study strategy, realizing they could make some use of it too.

The next morning, everyone began training again.

The changes were already in place, but their effect would only be felt in the latter half of their training. The beginning remained the same as before.

Mira’s intervention had been successful, decreasing the number of repetitive training Christina and the rest had to endure. But Helcune and her sisters were still struggling, as their skills were not yet as polished as the rest.

Meanwhile, Mira was checking how much Bruce had improved from the previous day.

He had been unsuccessful at taking down an Ashen Knight by relying purely on partial summoning, but the experience from his attempts had visibly helped him improve. Especially his shield usage was much cleaner and swiftly timed, showing just how desperate he had been to survive.

“Good good, I’d even say you’re combat ready in that aspect.”

Mira commented after seeing Bruce perfectly block an attack from a Dark Knight. But he was still a bit lacking when it came to partially summoning swords, he had improved his speed a bit, but it was not the best yet.

So Mira told him they would focus on that more, and summoned an Ashen Knight.

Bruce was initially delighted to receive praise for his shields, only to remember his ordeal from yesterday and all color drained from his face as he staggered backwards. Mira did not give him any time to recompose himself, mercilessly giving the signal to start and making Bruce train until he could barely move.

Past noon and lunch, they transitioned into studying strategy. Bruce, together with Helcune and her sisters, also joined that, as that knowledge could come in handy during the tournament, and it would help Bruce command his summons better in the long run too.

First, they began training with small groups.

The Valkyries would take command of the Dark Knights. Helcune and her sisters too, but as they did not have experience leading yet, they struggled a bit but did their best to keep up.

There were new types of troops too, with those with bows being led by Eletina, those with pikes by Shalwina, and those with battleaxes by Celestina.

That also meant that those three Valkyries would need to study more compared to the rest. On the other hand, more studying meant less time spent on Alfina’s harsh training. Since they were already among the more studious of the sisters, they were more than happy with the arrangement. And more importantly, they were delighted to do it for Mira.

Their days continued in a similar fashion, and soon a week had passed in the blink of an eye, so it was time for Mira and Bruce to leave.

Because of all the changes, it had also become common for everyone to gather in Mira’s room after dinner to ask for her opinion on various things they were studying.

Bruce’s training had also progressed decently, and he had reached the goal of taking down an Ashen Knight relying only on partial summons. Just like Mira had assured him, she had pushed him to a higher level in just a week.

Helcune and her sisters were still getting worn down every day, but they were slowly adapting to Alfina’s training. Physically, and more noticeably, mentally.

They also improved their strategy together with Bruce. Leading an army was still far too difficult, but they were good enough to move as a cohesive unit.

On the other hand, Alfina and her sisters were quickly adapting and incorporating the new forces into their training.

They already had experience fighting as an army, so it did not take them long. In particular, the barrages of arrows unleashed by Eletina’s archers were a sight to behold.

“Wanting to train hard is commendable, but remember to not overdo it.”

The Valkyries accompanied Mira and Bruce to the lowest island before they left in the morning, and Mira reminded them of that.

“Ahh…Master…we hardly deserve your kindness…”

The week Mira had spent there felt like a dream come true for Alfina, who was now overcome with emotion as Mira’s stay came to an end.

“Feel free to come visit again whenever you can, Master.”

Then, Christina said that with a cheerful voice. She was still grateful that Mira had helped make training more bearable, making her smile brightly. The rest of the sisters followed suit, having their own words to send Mira off.

Eletina fervently talked about researching more elemental magic to enhance the power of her archers, and to please summon her whenever it was appropriate to test it out.

She was always overly enthusiastic when it came to magic, but when she suggested that, everyone else wanted in as well, so in the end, Mira told them she would summon them once a week to train, after which they finally calmed down.

Then, Frodina brought up how she had started working on the seeds Mira gave her, with some already starting to sprout, and that she would keep updating Mira about it.

Shalwina had already read through all the comic books Mira had given her, so she was almost pleading with Mira to find new books for her whenever possible. She had also read through the entirety of the book from Solomon, memorizing its contents, so in the future, she would be directing their strategy and tactics training.

Elivina had also made progress with creating the improved armor. She had already woven some fabric with the materials Mira had given her, which turned out to be very pliable, while being far more heat, shock, and cut resistant than anticipated. It was the perfect material to use as padding below plate armor.

Celestina also mentioned how she was making good progress developing her special move, and was confident that she would be able to use it the next time they fought a strong foe together.

While Mira talked about those things with the seven sisters, Bruce was also talking with Helcune and her sisters.

They had already formed a strong bond, being able to live under the same roof and train together for some time. All of them were determined to continue working to get stronger together.

“Alright then, we’ll see each other again in a week.”  

“Thank you so much for everything.”

With those parting words, Mira and Bruce crossed the gate to leave Valhalla, descending back to their world.

It was possible to exit to a different place when leaving Valhalla, so Mira and Bruce chose to go to a different place from Ferz Island, picking a lake next to old ruins located close to Nirvana’s capital instead, bringing them closer to where the tournament would be held.

Once on the ground, they summoned Pegasus and Hippogriff and headed to the city.  

While flying, Mira began talking.

“Listen up, in the free-for-all, you never know who you will be pitted against. You’ll have to think of countermeasures for all situations.”  

“Huh…? Ah…! A-Alright…I’ll keep that in mind!”

She mostly meant to make small talk, and said that with a rather casual voice, but Bruce shuddered hearing that.

That was because he had only planned on taking part in the spellcasters division.

Being a member of the Tower, he was certainly amongst the top spellcasters. It was entirely possible he could win that division even. But the free-for-all was a different story. Most summoners, unlike Mira, were extremely weak in close range combat, especially against warriors.

It was only now that Mira mentioned the free-for-all that Bruce realized something, Mira had focused so much on teaching him partial summoning so he would be better equipped to deal against such warriors.

And so, at the very end, Mira shoved yet another problem into Bruce’s arms, who felt forced to take part in the free-for-all now, his eyes staring vacantly at the city they were flying to, while Mira continued talking with excitement about her dream of making summoners popular once again.

+++

# 309: Ratnatraya

Ratnatraya, the capital city of Nirvana. Mira remembered it as being quite a big city, and in the last thirty years it had only grown even more. A population of half a million seemed like a very safe estimate considering its size.

The streets were well taken care of, with plenty of street lights to make them safe even at night. The brick buildings lining the streets were also reminiscent of late nineteenth century London, making it easy to imagine Sherlock Holmes walking around there.

Only the enormous tournament arena stood out in the cityscape, next to which Mira and Bruce landed.

The scenery on the ground was also quite different, resembling the surroundings of a Colosseum. It was also filled with festive crowds, showing just how big of a deal the tournament was.

“Well then, I’ll leave the tournament in your hands. I don’t expect you to win if she takes part, but I hope you can make it up to the finals at least.”  

“I’ll try my best…”

There were many reasons why Mira had stayed for a week in Valhalla, but the main one was to get Bruce ready to perform well in the tournament.

It was still too early to tell whether they had accomplished that, but at the very least, Bruce was far stronger than when they first met. At least it was fair to say that he had gotten past his limits.

Mira was hopeful that Bruce would do well, painting summoners in a good light once again. She had been barred from participating in the tournament, so all the responsibility to do that rested on Bruce’s shoulders now.

There was also the likely chance that Meilin would take part, making it much harder for him to win. So Mira was just hoping for an impactful performance from his part to be satisfied.

“I’ll be seeing you around then. Also, here’s a farewell gift from me, and don’t neglect your daily training.”

This was as far as they would travel together, as further ahead was the tournament registration desk. But before leaving, Mira gave Bruce a notebook.

“What…is this?!”

Bruce took the notebook and looked through it, his eyes widening with shock. It contained information on how to further expand the skills he had learned in Valhalla. As Mira explained, his training was not over after that week, and she had thought of a training plan he could follow even while the tournament was ongoing.

“Thank you very much! I promise I’ll make good use of your teachings and study diligently!”

There was still some time before the actual tournament matches would start, so that notebook would allow him to keep training and become even stronger when the time came.

He had suddenly found himself enlisting into the free-for-all division, but now even he was starting to believe that he had a chance. But more importantly, he was delighted to be able to learn even more from one of the Nine Wisemen.

Since Bruce was going to participate in the tournament, he lined up to register. Mira went on a different way, quickly scouting the surroundings. Her main priority now was to find Meilin, assuming she was there.

There was still a week before the preliminaries, so at least Mira had ample time to search for her. Not to mention that with all the strong combatants that already gathered, there already were streetfights on a smaller scale happening nearby.

Knowing her, there was a high likelihood she was already embroiled in some sort of 1 vs. 100 fight somewhere. With that in mind, Mira began looking for the more hot headed crowds.

(It looks like it’s been a while since the last time there was a festival of this scale…)

There were countless stalls serving food or for other activities. Not everything was related to fighting either, there were quiz shows, fashion shows, orchestra performances, and things of the sort.

There was something for everyone to enjoy there, almost like a collection of all sorts of amusement spots.

Surrounded by all of that, it was only a matter of time before Mira got distracted, regardless of how strong her determination to search was.

(Mhmm… There’s no better companion than this when watching!)

Mira stood in front of a platform, holding a plate with various pastries in one hand, and a fruit sour cocktail on the other. She was watching a Magical Knights showcase, as they unveiled their new autumn collection.

On top of that, they also revealed their brand new line of clothing named Magical Lady, aimed at a more mature audience, which was received with thunderous applause. Those designs had a more intellectual and grounded appearance, with only a hint of whimsical flourishes.

(Ah, that looks like something Luminaria would be into.)

Those were Mira’s thoughts as she watched the show all the way to the end.

“Mira! I knew it was you!”

With the show over, Mira recalled she was supposed to be searching for Meilin and stood up, when someone suddenly called to her, someone who seemed to know Mira.

Wondering who that was, Mira turned around and saw a blonde lady, fully clad in Magical Girl style clothes.

“Hmm…you’re…”

She seemed familiar, but with Mira’s usual struggle at remembering faces, she could not pinpoint where she had seen that girl before. All Mira knew was that they had met somewhere.

Seeing Mira stunned in thought trying to remember, the lady decided to give her a hint to jog her memory.

“We sat together on the continental train, remember? I even took a picture of you for Magical Knights.”

She raised a camera and reenacted that moment. That finally made Mira remember, as she loudly exclaimed, “Ahhh! Yes, I remember now!”

But it was not enough for Mira to remember the lady’s name, so she had to **Examine** the lady before acting like she just recalled the name and said, “Theresa, right?”

“Aww, you remember? I’m so glad!”

Theresa smiled happily, then leaned in and lowered her voice to a whisper. “By the way…” she began, asking if Mira was the Spirit Queen who had recently been spotted in Sentopolly and Haxthausen.

“Yes, that’s me.”

Seeing no reason to hide the truth, Mira replied confidently. That only made Theresa beam even more as she exclaimed, “I knew it! Can I please take more pictures?!”

Around a month before, Theresa’s boss had somehow found the picture she took of Mira, and began wondering if that was actually the Spirit Queen.

That made Theresa’s boss become obsessed with the idea of utilizing Theresa’s familiarity with the Spirit Queen to turn her into one of their cover girls. It was all for Lyrical Knights, the magazine published by Magical Knights.

“Even though I’m just a public relations manager…”

Theresa grumbled and then looked at Mira, her eyes seeking salvation.

“That’s rough.”

Mira had to think about it for a bit, then replied, “I’ll give you ten minutes.” She felt like it was going to be a hassle, but she also felt bad for Theresa and wanted to help.

“Thank you, Mira!”

That made Theresa jump with joy.

Magical Knights already had an area reserved for photoshoots of models near there, so Theresa led the way and took Mira with her. Mira followed behind, shaking her head in disbelief.

There was someone not too far away who had overheard their conversation. That person smugly told a friend about it, saying that the Spirit Queen had just passed by them.

“Thank you so much Mira! My boss might actually be happy with me now.”

The photo session took around ten minutes, after which she made a call, and then smiled happily at Mira, while also looking relieved.

From that, it was easy to glean that she had just informed her boss that the shoot had been a success. And she also received confirmation that Mira would become the front page gravure of the next monthly issue of Lyrical Knights.

It seemed like her boss had been really insistent about the matter, as she was unnaturally happy to have accomplished that.

A front page gravure was also another sign that the culture of former players was permeating into this world. Theresa had also said it without much importance, showing just how commonplace magazines were now.

But Mira was still unsure of how to feel about being depicted in gravure shots when usually she only looked at them.

“Well, I’m happy for you then.”

At least Mira’s old acquaintance was happy, so that was enough. Now she wanted to resume looking around the festivities outside, or rather continue searching for Meilin, but she was not able to say anything.

“Ah, I almost forgot!”

Theresa raised her voice first, sounding alarmed about something.

“Hm? What is it? Were there more angles you wanted to capture?”

Mira asked that, her mind filled with vain thoughts that ten minutes were not enough to capture all of her cuteness. But it was a completely different issue.

“It completely passed my mind since I got so excited to see you again, but we didn’t even discuss your payment for the pictures…”

While Mira had been fully ready to do the shoot for free, Theresa offered her the quite handsome sum of half a million Rils.

“We always process payments through the Union when we work with adventurers, does that work for you?”

After Theresa explained that, Mira put on airs as if she had done that plenty of times before, confidently saying, “Yes, of course.”

Theresa added that the payment should be processed in a week.

As they talked about that, Mira noticed a lot of noise behind her, as preparations began for the next fashion show and the models began to change.

“That’s everything then. We’ll be here for the entire duration of the tournament, so drop by if you have the chance. I hope we can meet again soon, Mira.”  

“Mhm, I’ll keep that in mind.”

The shooting set was also used as a changing room, and the two were surrounded by women changing clothes as they said goodbye. Which meant that it would be strange for Mira to stay there after that.

So with her heart filled with regret, she had no choice but to leave.

(I feel like everyone is watching me.)

Around fifteen minutes after she left the Magical Knights’ show area, as she resumed her search for Meilin, Mira felt a strange sensation and looked around her. For some reason, a lot of people were turning to look at her after the photoshoot.

But soon enough, everything was cleared up, as a small girl accompanied by her parents ran up to Mira, her eyes twinkling as she asked, “Are you the Spirit Queen?”

“Yes, that’s me.”

Mira replied with a warm smile and patted the girl’s head. When she said that, there was a clear reaction from everyone around them.

So far, the only description of the Spirit Queen everyone knew was that she was a silver haired girl with blue eyes wearing Magical Girl style clothes.

Those features were not uncommon in this world, so it did not narrow down her appearance too much. There had not been any pictures of her published at a large scale either, so oftentimes she would not be recognized in public.

But now that word had spread that the Spirit Queen had been sighted around that area, everyone was on the hunt for a girl with those features, wondering if it was or not the Spirit Queen.

Even the little girl had thought the same.

Mira noticed how excited that girl was to meet the Spirit Queen, and decided to make her even happier by letting her ride on Pegasus and so on. Then, when it was time for the girl to leave, Mira did not forget to preach about summoners by saying, “Summons are incredible, right?”

All of that had the side effect of making Mira explode in notoriety, with more and more people trying to talk with her, and slowing her down considerably.

(I guess it’s about time I try out the disguise.)

She did not mind improving the perception of summoners like that, but soon, she would be overwhelmed and unable to move, impeding her search for Meilin.

So she began scouting her surroundings, thinking of disguising herself, all the while grinning and playfully grumbling about how troublesome being famous was. At least she was already prepared for such a situation, thanks to Solomon and the hair dye he had provided her with. But then she noticed her own shortsightedness.

“Hrm…”

She could not think of any suitable places to change in.

The first thought she had was a public toilet. But those were just that, toilets, facilities to take care of certain business, without proper changing and washing rooms.

Then she thought of the fitting room in a clothing store, but that also did not feel right. Those were meant for clients, something she was not.

So she thought of a place of her own, her wagon, a far more reasonable and realistic option compared to the others. Except that it also had a shortcoming.

Everyone was already looking at her, so they would notice her going into her wagon and someone else coming out, quickly making everything useless as they would realize she had disguised herself.

After some deliberating about it, she turned around and headed to the one place she saw as the best in her position.

+++

# 310: Black hair debut

“Oh, Mira! We meet again after just half an hour.”

Theresa greeted Mira, seeing her come running back so soon. That was the place Mira had thought of as the ideal place to disguise herself, the Magical Knights’ booth and photo shoot area.

“I’m sorry to impose, but could I borrow your changing room for a bit?”

After the request, Mira explained that she was currently trying to find a way to disguise herself. Theresa found the idea fun and agreed right away, securing a spot for Mira.

Theresa was also curious to see what kind of disguise the Spirit Queen had come up with, so she offered to help if necessary and went into the changing room with Mira.

“Let’s start with this then.”

Now that she had some quiet and peace to change, Mira took out the hair dye and stood in front of a mirror. The dye came in a black container around the size of a water bottle. She had never used it before, but Solomon had told her to just rub it on her hair.

“Ah, is that a Jenuslean black dye?! Amazing… You really know what to get!”

Before she could start, Theresa shouted in excitement behind her. She had heard about that type of dye before, or rather, was extremely knowledgeable about it.

“Oh…so that’s what it’s called.”

Theresa then added that all fanatics of dressing up, basically cosplayers, knew about that brand. Their pigments, color assortments, smell, and ease of use were all a step above the competition.

The only downside was their high cost. Just the bottle Mira had went for around 100,000 Rils.

“I can’t believe it…”

Mira’s usual stinginess reared its head the moment she heard the price, making her hesitate to use it. But she also knew that a change in hair color was key for her disguise to work, so she faced the mirror again, ready to dye her hair when she noticed something else.

She had never dyed her hair before, so she did not know where to begin. Solomon simply told her to rub it into her hair, but had not mentioned how much or how hard. Maybe just a light application was enough.

All she could do was uncap the bottle and stand still.

“Mira, please let me do it for you!”

That was when Theresa offered to help.

She had likely noticed Mira’s internal struggle…or maybe not quite. She just ran up to Mira and very excitedly asked to experience what it was like to use that high quality dye. She even tried her best to sell herself as a professional.

As a cosplayer herself, Theresa had experienced a lot, including dying her own hair dozens of times. She had also been hopeful to obtain a bottle of Jenuslean dye, preparing herself for that day, practicing how to use it and researching all she could. So she was confident she would be able to use it perfectly.

“Well, if you’re so confident then I’ll leave it in your hands.”

Mira replied, acting as if she had been impressed by Theresa’s claims, but in reality, she was relieved to have found a way out. It was better for someone with experience like Theresa to do it, rather than for Mira to do it for the first time. So she accepted right away.

“Thank you, Mira!”

Theresa was so happy she almost broke out dancing, quickly saying, “I’ll go bring my tools!” and running off somewhere. Then, a moment later, she was back, her footsteps echoing loudly as she ran back. She showed up with two large bags, filled to the brim, even though all she was going to do was dye Mira’s hair.

“That’s quite the assortment of tools you’ve got there…”  

“Being able to use Jenuslean dye on your hair is a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity after all!”

Theresa took out item after item from her bag, lining them up on a table. Her voice was also filled with enthusiasm, showing how much she was looking forward to doing it.

“Let’s go!”

Theresa took the bottle of Jenuslean dye from Mira very respectfully, then got to work very eagerly.

“Woah, it smells so nice!”  

“It feels so much smoother than I imagined.”  

“Ah, why is it so stretchy!”  

“I can’t believe it takes effect so quickly!”  

“I’ve never seen such a nice luster!”  

“Ahh…so this is the power of Jenuslean…”

She used all her tools in quick succession, carefully applying the dye to Mira’s hair. Just like she had claimed before, she was actually a professional, and Mira’s hair came out nothing short of perfect.

“Ohh, that does change my appearance a lot.”

Mira looked at Theresa’s masterwork in the mirror, being filled by a strange feeling that she was looking at someone else that was not her.

Her platinum-like hair now appeared like glossy obsidian, making her nearly unrecognizable. That change alone would help her blend in a lot now.

“I doubt I would’ve done such a good job on my own. You have my gratitude.”

Mira stood up satisfied and thanked Theresa, and she thanked Mira back for giving her the opportunity to experience something so unique. In the end, both had gained something from it.

“Alright, now I only need to change clothes.”

After one last look in the mirror, Mira knew that a change in clothes would make her unrecognizable, allowing her to focus on searching for Meilin. So she took out the disguise she had ready.

That was a set of clothes she had picked herself.

Clothes she determined were the best for a disguise. Lily and the maids had been planning something as well, but Mira knew that if she let them give her a disguise, they would create something overly flashy.

That defeated the purpose of a disguise, something normal meant to blend in with other people. So Mira had chosen to visit a clothing store herself, and pick something normal and plain.

“This way, no one will be able to tell it’s me.”

Mira quickly undressed and put on her disguise. Then she took it a step further, adding a pair of vanity glasses. She slipped them on, looked at herself in the mirror, and grinned, delighted by how perfect the look was.

“So how is it? Do you think anyone will notice it’s me?”

She turned around and asked Theresa’s opinion, full of confidence.

But Theresa awkwardly looked away, like she was trying to avoid facing reality or having to express her true impression. It took her a moment to forcefully compose herself, her cheek twitching as she tried to form a smile and reply, “No, I’m sure no one would know.”

“I know, right? I know!”

With Theresa’s support, Mira was sure she would be able to freely walk out in the open. “I’ll be seeing you then,” she said and began walking away.

Theresa watched in dismay, because in simple terms, the clothes Mira had picked were terribly out of fashion and mismatched. Obviously no one would think she was the Spirit Queen, they would all just assume she had led an unfortunate life.

“Mira! Wait!”

In the end, Theresa could not see her leave that way, so she called Mira to stop while trying to figure out a tactful way of fixing things. She did not want to hurt Mira’s feelings by calling out her poor sense of fashion, but she wanted to get her to change into a different outfit.

“Hm? What is it?”

Mira turned around, wondering why Theresa sounded so desperate, and she just forced a smile while replying.

“You know, we have a new lineup that is still being developed with the main idea being daily life. That fits perfectly with the disguise you want. So…I thought that maybe you could try it on now that you’re here? Just wait here for a moment, don’t even think of leaving!”

After Theresa explained that, and putting extra emphasis on her plea for Mira to stay, she ran out of the room.

“Hmm…I wonder what kind of outfit that is.”

Mira knew that Magical Knights was centered around the Magical Girl fashion style, so she was curious to see what they would come up with for more casual clothing. As such, she waited patiently just like Theresa had asked her to.

“I’m back, Mira!”

Some time later, Theresa returned, still rushing around like earlier. She brought with her a suitcase for clothes, which she opened and held up the contents for Mira to see.

“Ta-da! Here it is.”

It looked like a rather simple outfit. It was just a blouse decorated with a ribbon and a black skirt. Quite different from those shown off in the public event earlier.

“Ohh… You were right, this does look a lot more casual.”

There was nothing directly tying it to the Magical Girl style, simply looking like a cute and comfy regular outfit. Mira looked at it, impressed with the unexpected choice from Magical Knights.

Still, knowing that brand, she knew there had to be something more to the outfit and decided to ask Theresa about it.

“Umm…this is still an early prototype, so it’s supposed to stay secret within the company…”

With that initial warning, she spoke a little about the outfit. It was something recently suggested by the design team, based around the theme of daily clothes, but other options had gained more votes.

“The design is still being worked on to be more viable, so this is just a regular outfit stashed away. And you know…I started to think that it’d be sad if no one wore them at all, so…”

Someone had put a lot of effort into crafting that outfit, only for it to fail the next stage of production. Knowing it would end up collecting dust somewhere without ever being worn made her feel a bit guilty. Still, her main reason for bringing it was to stop Mira from stepping out in something utterly ridiculous.

That made for the perfect excuse to get Mira to wear it instead, so Theresa looked at her with pleading eyes.

“Hmm, alright. I’ll just have to wear it then!”

Mira accepted the whole story, and agreed without offering any resistance. That was partly because of the outfit, but also because she appreciated Theresa’s behavior quite a lot when compared to how the castle’s maids acted.

“Thank you, Mira!”

Seeing how happy Theresa was made Mira smile and say, “It was nothing,” before quickly changing into it.

Thanks to Theresa’s excellent skills, the outfit she brought was the perfect size for Mira and there was no need to adjust anything. And so, Mira went from clothes randomly cobbled together, into a plain yet cute outfit.

The secret behind those clothes she had refused to elaborate on was something that would only manifest once they were complete.

Namely, the ability to transform into Magical Girl style clothes. In short, they would have a built-in gimmick to perform a transformation scene.

+++

# 311: Search and Discovery

The combination of dyed hair, vanity glasses, and a new outfit made Mira impossible to identify as the Spirit Queen. Theresa also felt at ease seeing Mira leave the Magical Knights’ booth like that.

The search for Meilin resumed after that. Mira mostly checked the places where crowds gathered to watch stage fights play out. But after an hour or two of searching, there was no hint of Meilin anywhere.

That made her check other fights as well, just in case. There were plenty of hot blooded adventurers gathered there, so it made sense for brawls to break out everywhere, and the guards had their hands full trying to keep things in order.

“Hmm…I guess she isn’t in those fights after all.”

After checking around ten brawls, she decided those were not the place to search. As much as Meilin liked to fight, she also had a background in martial arts, making her value honor and proper manners, not mindless violence.

So with her priorities straightened out again, she focused on stage fights and smaller tournaments again.

All imaginable types of fights were being conducted on those, some being boxing matches, purely kicking based fights, swordsmanship contests with wooden swords, and even stranger ones like snowball fights.

She spent the next few hours looking at those. At times a famous adventurer would join them, sending the audience into a frenzy, but Meilin was nowhere to be found.

Time passed like that, and before she realized, the sun had set and the moon was shining bright in the sky.

Soon, everything began to shut down for the night, and some of the stage platforms that had been so crowded earlier were being disassembled. The visitors also began to leave one after another, so Mira decided to give up her search until the next day too.

(I’m certain she’s here…I just didn’t account for the size of this place.)

While it was true that she was constantly getting distracted and taking detours, searching the entire place at once was not realistic either way.

There was an enormous plot of land dedicated to the tournament and all the miscellaneous events nearby, making it essentially a large amusement park, with various attractions on different stages.

It did not matter how predictable Meilin was, there were way too many places where she could be at any given time. So Mira had to think of something else.

At least, walking around had shown her how effective her disguise was. No one had even thought of the Spirit Queen when seeing her, but on the other hand, she was now seen as an easy target for men.

Before, the possibility of her being the Spirit Queen had made her a beautiful girl surrounded by a powerful aura. But now, she was nothing more than a beautiful girl passing by.

“Hey, you! We’re about to get dinner, wanna come too?”  

“I’ve got somewhere to be. I’ll have to pass.”

She was constantly being hit on by men like that, and she always had to walk faster to get away before they could stop her. At least it was something she was used to by now.

She had also given up on her search for the night, so she strolled around there until she got to the exit. Signups for the tournament were still on-going, with plenty of people moving around.

(How should I search tomorrow, hmm…)

Realizing the scope of the search area, she knew continuing searching the same way would be futile, and she needed to think of a new plan for the next day.

“Huh? I also have to write down where I’m staying? I don’t know… All the inns I checked before were packed so I haven’t found a place yet.”  

“Ahh, in that case allow me to introduce you to an inn sponsoring the tournament. Take this card and show it to the owner and you should be able to get a room.”

Mira overheard that conversation, happening between an applicant and the clerk taking in signups.

(The place they’re staying at…is written there?)

That gave Mira an idea, and to make sure of it, she approached a nearby staff member. First, she asked what all the required information to sign up was. The staff member replied by examining Mira’s appearance with a bit of confusion, but then explained everything she would need.

There were various requirements, starting with the applicant’s name, age, class, and the place where they were staying.

Mira asked why they required that last point, and he replied that it was to have more information on how business was going for the various inns.

There were tens of thousands of participants and visitors coming to the city for the tournament, so they wanted to know how the inns were being managed, the places preferred by the visitors, whether they were being guided around properly, and so on. That was why they required that information.

(I see…so if I get my hands on the application forms, I should be able to find where Meilin is staying at.)

Knowing Meilin, the first thing she had done in the city was complete her application. She always had the habit of getting such procedures out of the way as soon as possible, and Mira was certain that Meilin would be taking part in the tournament.

Mira quickly made up her mind with that knowledge. She would check the application forms and figure out where to find Meilin.

As obsessed as Meilin was over martial arts, barely ever thinking of anything else, she had to know how much weight her name carried, so it was likely she had signed up with a fake name.

But Mira also knew her enough to know she would use a very simple name like Meimei, Linlin, or at most Linmei. Mira just had to look for names on that vein and Meilin would show up soon enough.

Her age was something a bit less reliable, since it was hard to know whether Meilin had been keeping count properly or not.

Then there was the class, something Mira believed would essentially pinpoint Meilin. Even if by some miracle Meilin had come up with an unpredictable fake name, the way she wrote her class would be a strong hit.

There was something Mira and Meilin had talked about way back in the past, during one of the times when Meilin was mentoring Mira. It was just a random comment, that since Meilin came from a family of martial artists, she might as well be a Martial Sage. Somehow, Meilin had really liked that, and began calling herself a Martial Sage from then onwards.

In her own words, that was a representation that she would take both martial arts and sage arts to the utmost level.

Mira recalled that exchange, and she was convinced that Meilin would also enroll as a Martial Sage for the tournament. It did not matter how many sages took part, that detail alone would single out Meilin.

The only issue was the application forms themselves. The clerks would obviously refuse to let her look through them if Mira asked. But this was Nirvana, so maybe there was a different way to get to them.

“By the way, it seems like you’ll end up getting piles of documents this way. Are you sure nothing will get misplaced?”

Mira decided to prod around a bit, and received exactly the response she wanted. The staff member she was talking to replied that the committee formed to run the tournament was directly archiving the applications for safekeeping, so there was no need to worry about anything being misplaced. In other words, Mira just needed to find that committee and she would get what she wanted.

“That’s reassuring to hear. Sorry for taking your time.”

She had gained the information she wanted, and now she knew where to go next, so she thanked the staff member and left.

The whole tournament was the biggest national event so far, so the committee running it had also been formed and was overseen by the government.

With that in mind, her connections would do the heavy lifting.

(I don’t like having to say that I’m me, but it seems they already found out, so I might as well endure a moment of shame.)

She would need the committee’s permission to look through the applications. The fastest way to accomplish that was by talking to high ranking officers in the government, and Mira just so happened to be friends with someone like that. Then, there was the fact that she had been preemptively restricted from taking part in the tournament, being instead invited to be a commentator, which overall meant that someone there had realized that Mira was Danbulf.

All of that combined would speed things up.

(I might even get a place to stay too.)

The conversation she had overheard earlier also told her that searching for an inn with empty rooms would be a back breaking ordeal. But she had been invited as a commentator, so the least they could do for her was to give her a place to stay. With that in mind, she headed straight for the imperial palace.

The residential area close to the palace had mansions built with excellent masonry, the streets were paved with stone, and lined with beautiful trees. There were plenty of street lamps too, providing ample illumination to the areas where nobles resided and gathered. All of that was still largely the same as Mira remembered from thirty years in the past.

It was also night already, so most people were staying inside their homes, so only a few servants running errands or guards on patrol could be seen on the street.

“Okay…I can move now.”

Mira watched a guard pass by and waited a moment before emerging from the shadow she was hiding in and continued sneaking forward. She was afraid that if someone saw her walking around alone so late, they would take her into protective custody.

So she moved forward while avoiding contact with others as much as possible, especially the guards, making her seem like some sort of burglar.

(Now that I think about it, I should let Solomon know about this first.)

As she got closer to the palace, she thought of something. If she requested to see the application forms, they would indubitably want to know the reason why. She could simply say that she was looking for Meilin, but the issue was that her search for Meilin and the remaining Nine Wisemen was supposed to be a top secret matter. Even if they were close friends, Nirvana was still a separate country, so it was better if Mira asked for Solomon’s permission first.

That meant using the communications device in her wagon, which was not really a big problem to get to. Only to realize that she would quickly stand out if a wagon suddenly showed up in the streets where nobles lived.

She did not want to have to explain things to the guards there, so instead, she began looking for a more hidden place where she could get into her wagon in peace.

(I think there was a park somewhere nearby…)

Assuming the layout of the city had not changed, there had to be a large park near there, so Mira began heading in that direction. It was known as the National Evergreen Forest Park, made to look like an actual forest.

The park was located in the very center of the city, and had a square shape with each side measuring one kilometer, being surrounded by densely packed streets.

During the day, people would go through the hiking trails in it, and the various resting spots were well known as good spots for dates. But at night, it gave off a completely different appearance.

The entrance was lined with cherry trees, covered with green leaves. During the morning light would trickle down through the leaves, creating a relaxing atmosphere. And during Spring, the cherry trees would be in full bloom, soothing one’s very soul.

Currently, it was almost Fall, so the branches were densely packed with leaves, creating strong shadows and darkness, with some spots seemingly untouched by light.

(This seems perfect for tests of courage.)

Those were the thoughts circling in Mira’s head as she walked through the path. And then she caught sight of a moving light, different from the lamps illuminating the path, so she shuddered for a moment. But after getting a closer look, she eased up.  

It was a guard patrolling the park.

“Someone’s taking their job too seriously…”

Mira grumbled to herself as she ran away from the path, hiding amongst the trees before the guard noticed her. Then, she used Life Sensing to make sure the guard was gone before coming out again.

(Maybe it’s better if I go further in.)

The guard was carefully looking around, but only around the path and did not check behind the trees. Still, it was better to avoid any place that could be spotted from the path. So Mira headed further away, trying to find a place where the trees grew more densely.

The trees in the park had been manually planted instead of letting them multiplicate naturally, so it was hard to find a spot where they grew densely enough to offer coverage from patrolling guards.

(Hmm…this could work.)

Eventually, Mira found an unused management hut deep within the artificial forest, which offered just enough cover. It was also a distance away from the main path, with the way leading there looking more like an animal trail. There were also piles of scrap wood, creating more blindspots.

She quickly opened her Item Box to take out her wagon, but then realized that doing that would create flashes of light as the spells activated, so first, she used Life Sensing to scout her surroundings in case there was a guard nearby.

(Hm..! Who’s there?!)

She got two large readings, on the other side of the hut around thirty meters away from her. They were clearly too big to be animals, so she was sure they had to be people.

At first, she thought they were guards, but soon thought differently, as a third reading showed up and joined the first two.

The way that third one moved did not make sense for a guard either, and resembled more the way Mira herself had navigated the forest thus far. Hiding behind trees and constantly stopping to look around. Once all three were together, they just stood still.

All she could tell was that they seemed to know each other, but she still wondered just what they could be doing in such a place so late at night.

(Are they actually thieves?)

The park that was so beautiful during the day was surprisingly quiet and somber at night. It was also surrounded by mansions where nobles and important people lived. There were only a few reasons Mira could think of that would explain those three convening in secret in such a place, making her look at them with suspicion.
