“Well…yes, I guess so.” Mira was a bit dizzy from how fast things were moving, but she was meaning to talk about all that anyway, so she took the device.

‘Hello, this is Solomon.’ A few seconds later, the call connected and Solomon’s voice came through the device.

“It’s me, it’s me!”  

‘Ahh, I see. So how’s it going? Did you find any leads?’

Mira’s way of speaking was enough for Solomon to know who it was, as his voice became far more relaxed and casual.

“About that…”

Mira quickly summed up everything that had happened so far, then mentioned that she was calling from Alma’s room, that Esmeralda was also there, and that she needed to reveal her mission to proceed.

‘I see. Alma already knows about our situation, so I don’t mind if you tell her.’

When Mira was done explaining, Solomon did not sound too concerned about it. Even if the mission was a state secret, the two countries were on friendly terms and there was enough trust between them to share the information.

‘Is that all? I’ll leave you to talk then.’  

“Thank you Solomon! I’ll call you again later!”

As soon as the call was over, Alma and Esmeralda’s eyes locked on Mira. She was really feeling the pressure from both of them, but since Solomon had given her his blessing, she began talking.

“So the truth is…”

Mira began telling her about her secret mission, interrupted from time to time with snack breaks. In short, she was searching for the Nine Wisemen to bring them back to Arkite.

“Ohh, so you’re already working on that! I was getting worried for Solomon, but with Grandpa on the case, I’m sure everything will sort itself out!”

Alma had been worried for a while that Luminaria was the only Wiseman present, so she was relieved and excited when she heard that Mira was working on fixing that. A moment later, a certain expectation mixed with worry clouded Alma’s face as she hesitantly asked something.

“So…how’s it going? Your search, I mean. Do you happen to know anything about Fumika…I mean Artesia?”

Artesia was Alma’s sister-in-law. Or to be specific, Alma was the younger sister of Artesia’s late husband. They had been very close to each other for a long time, with Alma treating her like a real older sister, so it was no surprise that Alma was worried about her.

“Actually, I do know, Artesia is…”

Artesia’s location was yet another state secret, and Mira had only received permission to talk about her mission itself, not her current progress. But knowing Alma and Artesia thought of each other as family, she decided to tell Alma everything.

Artesia had been found around two months before, and was currently leading a newly instated orphanage in Lunatic Lake. Her return was still kept secret and would only be announced to the public during the celebration of Arkite’s foundation anniversary.

+++

# 317: Special ticket

“I see, so she’s living surrounded by children. At least I’m glad she’s happy then.” Alma looked relieved when she heard how Artesia was doing now.

Esmeralda was also happy for her, beaming a delighted smile. But as she was a fellow saint, she also began to wonder if Artesia had gotten any stronger.

Artesia the Rivalrous and Esmeralda the Divine Herald, one was one of the Nine Wisemen, the other one of the Twelve Apostles. Both were saints, but they had developed their skills in different directions.

Artesia had focused the most on healing and defense, while Esmeralda was better at strengthening and attacking. That was also influenced by the country they belonged to, and the friends they surrounded themselves with.

Solomon from Arkite’s team could serve as a tank, but everyone else barely knew what defending meant, so Artesia focused on filling that blank.

Meanwhile, Nirvana’s team had plenty of members with a warrior class, who naturally had more resilient bodies. And instead they had very few spellcasters, so Esmeralda tried to find a way to attack even as a saint to balance out their damage types.

“Could I go see her…” Alma mumbled those words, her voice filled with nostalgia, longing, and a bit of hope.

“Hmm, that might be difficult.”

Mira was the first to reply, followed by Esmeralda, “Sadly, you would need a major reason to leave the country.”

Thinking about it more rationally, it was not right for an empress to leave her country simply to go meet with one person. The only possible way would be as a diplomatic visit to Arkite as a whole, but the tournament happening in Nirvana was far too big of an event for Alma to be absent.

Then there was the option of calling Artesia to come visit Nirvana instead, which had its own difficulties. Artesia would never leave all of the children of the orphanage, no matter how badly Alma wanted to see her.

Alma and Esmeralda were fully aware of Artesia’s nature when it came to children, so they did not even have to bring up that option.

“Actually, there might be a way.”

Anyone with a heart would want to let them meet even more knowing all of those circumstances, so Mira gave it some serious thought until she came up with a solution.

“Really?!”

Alma latched onto that possibility instantly, and Esmeralda also looked hopeful at Mira. With both of them paying attention to her, Mira prefaced her response by saying that she did not know if Nirvana had the necessary means yet.

“You know, if the mountain won’t come…or however that saying goes.”

Alma leaving the country was already ruled out, so they had to focus on ways to get Artesia there instead, which could work if they invited not just Artesia but everyone in the orphanage.

The tournament happening in Nirvana also gave them the perfect reason to do that. There were plenty of things for the children to see and enjoy in the city. And if visiting would make the children happy, then Artesia would never deny them that enjoyment, meaning she would readily accept.

Once they were in the city, Alma would just have to open a spot in her schedule for a meeting.

“The crucial part is how you invite them here. If you single out one orphanage to give them special treatment, other places might not appreciate it, no?”

Mira wrapped up things with that warning. Being given preferential treatment by a large country like Nirvana would raise all sorts of questions and doubts. If Alma did not handle that carefully, things could get dangerous, or some might even uncover Alma’s and Artesia’s personal relationship.

There was also the fact that the orphanage had only been set up recently, so it was better to avoid shining a spotlight on them. Regardless, Mira still sympathized with Alma’s feelings, and offered to help in any way she could.

Having heard Mira’s idea, Alma remained silent for a while, deep in thought. A few minutes later, her whole face lit up as she exclaimed, “Yes, that might work!”

“Oh, have you thought of a tactful way of inviting them?”

Mira asked just to confirm, and Alma nodded brimming with confidence.

“I’ve recently joined a trade route through Sentopolly, thanks to Solomon’s intervention. I’ve wanted to do that ever since I heard they had managed to build a port in those tall cliffs on the western shore more than a decade ago, but they wouldn’t listen to me until Solomon put in a word for me. So maybe I could send a written invitation to Arkite as a token of gratitude for making that possible? And couple that with my best wishes for the newly instated orphanage.”

After saying all that, she looked at Esmeralda with expectant eyes.

“I can’t deny that it sounds rather forceful. But you have a track record of being generous towards orphanages in the past, so we can just wave it away like that. Nothing to see here, just our empress’ usual quirks creeping up.”

When Esmeralda mentioned that, Alma looked away.

Maybe Artesia’s habits had rubbed off on her, or maybe she was always like that, but Alma was always overbearing whenever children came into the picture, but not to the same extent as Artesia. Essentially, if she saw a kid crying, she would not move on until she did something about it.

That was only an issue because Alma was also the empress, having a lot of authority at her disposal, and judging by Esmeralda’s reaction, Alma had caused quite a few scenes in the past because of that.

“Hmm, that might work, yes. If I may suggest one just thing, Arkite has another orphanage in Caranach, so it would be wise to consider that too.”

Alma’s idea would probably stave off envy from other countries. But singling out one orphanage within Arkite would not paint a good picture. When Mira mentioned that, Alma instantly said, “Then I’ll just invite that one too!”

“Well, that solves that…”

An invitation was easy to write, but fulfilling it would incur various costs. Just transporting one of them would be considerably expensive, but Alma did not worry about that in the slightest.

“Let’s see…how much for a round trip from Arkite…”

She quickly jotted down an estimate on a notebook, starting with the transport costs.

“Grandpa, would you happen to know how many children there are?”  

“I’m pretty sure there were a hundred with Artesia, and in Caranach I don’t have the slightest idea. I’d say below a hundred would be a good estimate though, judging by how big it is.”

Mira replied to Alma’s question as best as she could, also adding that there were around ten adults helping Artesia watch over the kids in her orphanage.

“Hmhm…so that’s all of them. I think a medium sized flying ship would be enough…”

One step after another, the plan was taking form. Alma even brought up flying ships without a second thought, a really expensive commodity that only a few countries could manage to own a single one. But Nirvana was far larger and powerful than most, and considering Alma could classify them in different sizes, she probably owned multiple of them.

(I was thinking of asking Kagura for help again if transport became an issue…but I guess I never had to worry about that…)

Mira was starting to feel vertigo at the staggering power of Nirvana and Alma, and decided to just watch and wait until the plan was complete.

Inviting an orphanage or two from another country to visit Nirvana seemed like a trivial matter for the empress of Nirvana. And what shocked Mira the most was that she was planning on paying for everything from her personal savings instead of her country’s funds.

“…There’s still an empty mansion in the clerical district, right? I guess they could stay there.”  

“Yes, that place is still empty. And it should be big enough to house two hundred children.”

Esmeralda also offered some advice when necessary, and soon they were bringing up nine digit sums for the total cost of the trip, which did not seem to bother Alma in the least. By that point, it was Mira who began to feel nervous, as she had come up with the idea first.

“…Alright, I think this is good enough. We’ll get everything moving first thing tomorrow morning.”

It only took around ten minutes to wrap up their planning session. It was clear that both Alma and Esmeralda were keenly familiar with everything going around in Nirvana, a country they had been leading for more than thirty years, so it made sense they had the experience that went with that.

“Are you done now? Then can we move on so I can finally know why you invited me all the way here?”

While they were planning, Mira had been liberally reaching out for the tea and snacks on the table, and she was still eating as she spoke to the two. After all, initially she had been told that she would hear more about those assassins when she was led there.

“Ah, you’re right. Sorry for getting distracted.”

Alma looked at the notes she took, satisfied with her plan, and then quickly gave a fake cough to change topics.

“_Ahem_, well, actually I wanted to ask if you could watch over our Oracle.”

After sitting up straight, Alma made that request, which only confused Mira.

All she had heard so far was that the leader of those assassins had been a man called Jorg, who was part of some organization. She had been expecting to be told more about that organization, or maybe even tasked with bringing it down.

Instead, she was given the task of watching over someone. Amidst her confusion, she realized she had heard that word before.

The three assassins she had first encountered had also been targeting some Oracle, who they said could see the future in some way, and had ruined a lot of business deals for their organization.

“Would that happen to be…”

Recalling that, Mira went straight to the point as she asked in return, “…An Oracle that has the ability to see the future? And that’s who I have to protect?”

“Oh, so you already knew that much?”  

“I heard those assassins talking about someone like that.”

Alma was a bit shocked to hear that much, and Mira added, “They kept crying about how they could not even find a shadow of the Oracle,” while chuckling about it.

“And that’s because we have her hidden really well.” Alma also grinned hearing that, proud of herself. As she explained, the existence of the Oracle was treated as top secret, with almost no one knowing about the matter.

“The only ones who know about the Oracle with those powers are a handful of my high ranking officers, and one other person. He Who Commands the Dark Routes, August Gradin.”

Her gaze became sharper as she spoke that name, becoming almost chilling. It was not out of disgust or hatred, but a strong enmity.

“He Who Commands the Dark Routes…? I’ve never heard of him. What kind of person is he?”

That was the first time Mira had heard that name. She could only assume that it was someone deeply involved with the organization she had heard about, and she felt like it would become a long conversation, so she reclined back on the couch in anticipation.

Once Esmeralda brewed some more tea, Alma went into more detail about everything.

That organization had been lingering in the shadows of not just Nirvana, but many other countries, not too different from Chimera Clauzen in the past, which Mira and the Fifty Bells had taken down together. And there were sure to be more of such organizations out there.

This one, which had spread quite far, was called Ira Muerte, and Alma had been working on destroying it for some time already.

“After many years of investigation, we found out that there’s four heads leading the whole organization.”

With that prelude, Alma went on to explain who those four heads were.

One of them was in charge of the organization’s weapons and drug trade team. And the main difference between that team and any other merchants was that every single item they dealt with was mired in darkness.

Stolen goods were par for the course, then came concealed and illegal weapons, favored by everyone leading such underground lives. They also dealt with outlawed magic wares, and various types of poison and venoms.

Those items had no decent use, they only served to assassinate, assault, or kill for joy, always connected to death in one way or another. Even most other arms dealers would feel chills seeing those items.

“Some people really are twisted…”

Mira looked down with a pensive look after hearing some of the examples Alma gave of the damage caused by that organizations, like a time when some bandits spread poison and killed everyone in a town, righteous nobles being assassinated by their concealed weapons, or an entire forest that burned down together with the wildlife in it.

“Yes, and very much so.”

Alma agreed in a low voice. She made sure to stress that those were only a handful of examples, and not even the worst ones. Many of the crimes happening all across the continent had been facilitated by the items sold by that organization.

Mira was left without words hearing all of that.

+++

# 318: Ira Muerte

“Now, the second head…”

After taking a deep breath, she continued detailing the team led by the second head, which was also involved in illegal trade. Unlike the first team, however, this one dealt not in goods, but in lives.

“That scum will do anything from poaching to abducting and even murder.”

They not only poached endangered and protected animals, but would harm Sacred and Spectral Beasts, and obviously humans too.

They had no respect for wildlife sanctuaries and disregarded all of the preservation laws put in place by the Three Gods Countries. They also had no qualms about abducting children, and they would slaughter the parents if they got in the way.

And to really drive home how little they thought of human lives, if they were unable to sell their prey, they would mercilessly kill it.

“Hmm… That’s just pure evil…”

Mira winced with disgust hearing everything Alma told her. Sometimes the young Sacred Beasts they would poach would get injured in the process, becoming worthless in the market, also leading to their unnecessary death. There were also countless children who had been taken away from their parents by that team. All they left behind was anguish and tragedy.

“But I can actually give some good news about them too.” With that, Alma added, “What you did a while back dealt a pretty big blow to them,” grinning a little.

“A while back…? Did I do anything like that?” Mira just tilted her head in confusion, trying to understand what Alma was referring to. Eventually, she clarified that it was about Chimera Clauzen.

“You see, this team was closely tied to Chimera Clauzen, since they also sold a bunch of spirits.”

The destruction of Chimera Clauzen had also extended into that organization. As the Fifty Bells went around crushing any remnants of Chimera Clauzen, they also gained information about their associates, like that team.

The Fifty Bells also had excellent methods of interrogation, so it did not take long before they were tearing quite deep into that team.

Sensing their impending destruction, that team decided to cast off a large number of members and bases, cutting ties from Ira Muerte to spare the rest of the organization. So while they were being hunted down by the Fifty Bells from one side, their lifeline was also cut on the other side.

“Ohh, I hadn’t thought of that. At least my hard work paid off then.”

Mira was rather pleased with herself hearing that her work had such an effect somewhere else.

Following Chimera Clauzen’s destruction, they had no one to sell spirits to anymore, and the follow-up investigations also destroyed their ability to sell other beings.

It was almost shocking how quickly the number of intruders in sanctuaries and the casualties amongst Sacred Beasts had decreased. The same applied to human trafficking, with numbers decreasing so suddenly it was almost like something else had happened.

With all that combined, Alma thought it was safe to assume that everyone in that team was standing on hot water.

“Now, the third head’s team is actually the one you’ll be dealing with, Grandpa…”

Moving along, Alma detailed the team led by the third head of Ira Muerte.

That third team was deeply linked to the previous two.

Namely, they were in charge of distribution and transport. They would collect the weapons and items from the first team, as well as the animals and hostages from the second, and distribute them across the continent. He Who Commands the Dark Routes, August Gradin, was also the leader of that whole team.

“Ah, and this August is also a really messed up individual.”

August was also one of the few people aware of the existence of the Oracle, and Esmeralda stepped in to talk about him.

As his nickname suggested, he was the person controlling most of the underground trading routes across the continent. He had established them to transport illegal goods, which most bandits and evildoers relied on. That also meant that he oversaw any major trade deal that happened.

Everyone in the blackmarket knew about him, and that also meant that he oversaw Chimera Clauzen’s business deals.

“And you see, you’re not the only one who’s been hard at work, Grandpa. Keep this between us, but my army has actually managed to seize most of the underground trade routes he controlled.”

Alma looked almost smug about it, clearly glad of how much she had accomplished already. But what she had said would require an immense amount of effort to accomplish.

“…You say it like it was no big deal…but did you actually do that?”

Mira could not help but ask that, seeing Alma’s attitude. But that doubt was understandable, as so far it had been established that Ira Muerte was one of the biggest underground organizations, with connections all across the continent. And yet, Alma claimed to have seized almost all of their trade routes.

That equated to cutting their lifeline, as no matter how much of their wicked merchandise they gathered, it was useless if they could not sell it.

Mira could not comprehend how something like that was even possible.

“Mhm, it’s all true. By now I’ve probably ruined about…five hundred billion Rils worth of trade for them. And that’s where you come into the picture, Grandpa.”

Alma reaffirmed her claim, even mentioning an unimaginable sum of money, before she finally began talking about her request for Mira to guard the Oracle. After all, it was only thanks to the Oracle’s powers that Alma had been able to cripple Ira Muerte so much.

“You’ve heard she has the power to see the future, but that’s not very accurate. There’s clear limits and restrictions to her power, and it’s not like she can predict earthquakes or major disasters like that. To put it simply, her power…”

The Oracle’s power worked only on other people, greatly limiting the scope of her ability. On top of that, it was not as much of seeing the future, but more like seeing what the person was currently doing, _or what they were about to do_. That was the real power of the Oracle.

“And there’s one condition to activate that power in the first place. The Oracle needs to touch a prized possession of the target, or a piece of their hair or nails. Once one of those is secured, she can repeatedly use her power as many times as she wants. So…in other words, August is compromised and can’t do anything at all for the organization, or know anything about it anymore.”

Nirvana had been fighting against Ira Muerte for many years now, and a few months prior they had managed to find one of their bases, thanks to the efforts of many spies and soldiers. When they investigated the place, they were able to collect a vital item, a strand of hair from August.

“The benefit of that ability is that it works repeatedly. Once the Oracle touched the hair, and continued to touch it, she could tell what August was doing and planning, everything. So as long as we have the hair and the Oracle, he can’t do any work for Ira Muerte.”

Saying that, Alma’s eyes seemed to fill with pride. She was proud from the bottom of her heart about those serving her, whose continuous efforts had allowed her to deal such a major blow to Ira Muerte.

“I see… He knew about all the business conducted by the organization, so the Oracle’s power became his greatest weakness.”

August controlled the underground trade routes, used by Ira Muerte and many others, and all the information he obtained was channeled straight to the Oracle.

That meant that Nirvana also learned about other clients of August’s, who were also prosecuted and imprisoned, greatly decreasing August’s reputation and credibility. And whenever he tried to come up with countermeasures, Nirvana immediately knew about them.

The Oracle had left one of the biggest leaders of the organization hamstrung, leaving a devastating effect on everyone else.

Having heard that much, Mira understood why they had such a grudge against the Oracle, and was not surprised that they had sent assassins, it was almost expected at that point.

“By the way, there’s something I still don’t understand. Earlier you said only a handful of high ranking officers _and_ August know about the Oracle.”

Mira had a decent idea of the situation now, but there was one thing still bothering her, so she asked, “How come he found out about the Oracle in the first place?”

As far as she could tell, the assassins did not have any leads as to the Oracle’s whereabouts, some even doubted she existed in the first place. In short, she was perfectly hidden.

But Alma had claimed that August did know about her.

Everything Mira had heard indicated an untraceable method. A fallen strand of hair was enough to activate that power, and no one could plan against it without knowing of it beforehand. And yet, there had been assassins searching for the Oracle.

Mira wanted to know if there had been a leak of information somewhere, or how they had found out in the first place.

“You could probably think of it like a secondary effect… And I mean, it makes sense that such a powerful ability also has its downsides.” Alma began replying to Mira’s question, hydrating her throat with some tea before explaining what those downsides were.

The Oracle’s power was to read the target’s thoughts, see what they were doing and what they were about to do, all in great detail.

That involved delving deep into one’s thoughts, which would trigger a subconscious reaction from the target, who would also sense they were being observed and with what intentions.

“That’s true, we ran a few tests before to know how strong the effect was, and it was a really weird feeling.”

At some point, they had tested the Oracle’s powers on Esmeralda, who described the experience as being just an odd feeling at first, but after repeated use, she was able to sense the Oracle’s intrusion very clearly.

By now, the Oracle had used her powers on August more than a hundred times, so he should also be quite aware of what was happening. So it made sense that he and those around him decided to try getting rid of the Oracle.

“I see…so the target of this Oracle of yours figured out what was going on. Then why do you need me to guard her now? If you know all this much, then I’m sure you’ve already given her plenty of security.”

Alma had chosen to use the Oracle’s powers to close down the underground trading routes of Ira Muerte, despite the fact that they would learn about the Oracle in return. That was how important it was to shut them down.

They had already done a lot to keep the Oracle’s existence and her location secret, but the sensible choice was to also have tight security around her, and Mira knew that Alma was smart enough to be aware of that. Which was why she wondered why she had to step in to guard the Oracle now.

“Well, I mean… Yes, she is being guarded at the moment, but…”

As soon as Mira asked that, Alma began to stutter a little, looking around awkwardly.

She confirmed that the Oracle had been heavily guarded from the start, maybe even by one of the Twelve Apostles, considering how important the Oracle was. That would mean there was no reason for Mira to take over. Except that Alma did not sound too convinced about their current arrangement.

“Exactly what are you trying to say? Be a bit more clear.”

Mira urged Alma to explain things properly, while Alma struggled to find the right words, as she would open her mouth a bit and then fall silent right away time and time again.

“Just what is it?”

Just as Mira was starting to get annoyed, Esmeralda let out a deep sigh.

“Let me explain then.”

Seeing that things were going nowhere, Esmeralda felt like she had no choice but to step in, even if she also looked a bit hesitant to talk about it. Still, there was a need to explain why Mira’s help was needed, even if they had enough guards.

“You see, her current bodyguard is Noin.”

That was how Esmeralda began her explanation, but hearing that name only made Mira question things even more.

“What, then you can’t ask for a better bodyguard, can you?”

Noin the White Vault, one of the Twelve Apostles. He was a paladin just like Solomon, but he went on the proper and usual path of paladins, unlike Solomon who came up with his own way to fight.

He poured all his efforts into defense, and if he went all out, he could fend off even Isenfald’s Dragon Breath.

There had been a time when Danbulf and Noin fought a duel, which lasted for many hours without an end in sight, leading to it ending as a draw. With Isenfald’s attacks neutralized, all Danbulf could do was to use his army to stop Noin from moving. And in return, Noin was too busy fending off the army of summons and could not take a single step closer to Danbulf.

In the end, that stalemate was never broken, and their duel ended in a draw.

In short, no matter what type of attack came, or how many assassins made their way in, they would never be able to go through Noin to reach the Oracle, keeping her completely safe.

“I can’t see a world where I’d be of any use if that’s the case.”

Mira still could not comprehend why she was asked to help with that. Just what was the issue? If anything, Noin was far better qualified than her, so she just glared at Esmeralda wondering if they were just messing with her.

“I mean…at one point yes, that would’ve been true, but things have changed.”

Esmeralda looked away as she stumbled on her own words. But she understood that Mira would just keep demanding to know more, so she took a deep breath before trying to be more clear.

“You see…she…the Oracle is still a young girl…and umm…she’s become afraid of men…like a phobia… That’s why she becomes restless if Noin is near her, or even just in the same room… Now he can only stand watch outside of her room, but that means…you know…”

Esmeralda looked really troubled about having to say that, but at least that explained why Noin was no longer the ideal bodyguard choice, if anything were to happen, he would not be able to help to the best of his ability.

Meanwhile, Mira had more questions now. The way Esmeralda said it made it sound like the Oracle had not always had that phobia, and something had caused it to manifest.

There was a chance it was something Noin had caused, after all, he was a well known skirt chaser. But he also respected women, and would never intentionally do something to upset them.

On top of that, he really nailed the look of a paladin, so even if the Oracle fell in love with him, that should not be any reason for her to become afraid of men as a result.

“Hmm…a phobia towards men, huh… And how did that even happen?”

Mira was straightforward, as she wanted to know why that had happened so suddenly. Her curiosity was justified, as gaining a phobia so strong that it impeded the presence of a bodyguard was something strange.

But Esmeralda did not seem too thrilled to talk about it, and Alma continued to look away awkwardly.

Mira began to guess that it had been some really horrible experience, and decided she would tell them they did not have to say anything if they did not want to. But before she could say anything, Esmeralda took another deep breath and began talking.

“It was actually because of August…”

She once again spoke with constant pauses, and the story she told stunned even Mira.

When August realized that the Oracle’s abilities allowed her to see everything he was doing and planning, he decided to act in the worst way possible. Esmeralda’s face reddened as she related that, an endless onslaught of things children should never know about.

Basically, August had started engaging in the most perverse of fetishes with all sorts of women, all so the Oracle would also end up seeing that.

As Esmeralda explained, the Oracle was still of the tender and impressionable age of fourteen years old, so it was almost expected for such a young girl to gain a phobia after seeing all the dirty perversions carried out by August.

But if they stopped observing August, they would not know what was happening with Ira Muerte, and he would be able to go back to working as usual.

All they could do for the Oracle’s sake was to reduce the frequency with which she used her powers. That way, at least they could keep track of the bigger schemes within the organization, even if they lost the ability of gaining more granular information.

“What a sleazebag…”

That was the countermeasure August had taken as soon as he felt the Oracle was a girl. It was a rather ridiculous strategy, but he kept going when he noticed it had an effect. It was hard to tell whether he was doing it purely to fight back or if that was his true nature, but regardless, it was something Mira did not appreciate in the least.

+++

# 319: The objective of the tournament

“Now I understand why you asked me to do this. But don’t you have anyone else who isn’t male that could do it? I mean, there’s Emeko right next to you too.”

Since the Oracle was afraid of men, it made sense that Mira, who was a girl in body at least, would be a better bodyguard. But Mira still had some doubts. There were plenty of other females amongst the Twelve Apostles, so one of them would also be a good replacement.

Alma was the one to answer that question.

“Usually, that’d be the case, but I’m a bit short of hands at the moment.”

Alma nodded, agreeing with Mira’s opinion, but then explained why she could not do it this time. All the other Twelve Apostles other than Noin were busy with their own missions.

As she said that, Alma began grinning more, in an almost devilish way which was rather unbefitting of an empress, but in her mind, she was probably trying to smile in a more scheming way. Regardless, the confidence she beamed made Mira wait to see what more she would say, instead of urging her to get to the point.

“You see, I organized this tournament with a specific goal in mind. Which happens to be an important step towards taking down Ira Muerte!”

Mira thought she would learn what the other female members of the Twelve Apostles were doing, only for the conversation to deviate into yet another unexpected direction.

But because it seemed so unrelated, it ended up circling around to become connected again in some form.

The tournament that was happening in Nirvana was actually one of many simultaneous plans being carried out to smoke out and destroy all of the top members of Ira Muerte.

“…So basically everyone else already has their hands full. And we two are also busy preparing the best stage possible.”

They were up against one of the biggest underground organizations in the continent, and even a large empire like Nirvana had a hard time dealing with them. So instead they prepared various secret plans to lure Ira Muerte into a better position.

In short, the tournament was merely a front to gather as many people from all over the world into one spot, which could be dangerous, but also would allow them to catch a bunch of Ira Muerte’s top members in one swoop.

“I see… So that’s why everyone is busy.”

Another part of that plan was to invite various important officials from other countries to the tournament as well. Not just any officials, but ones who had a secret in common, though it was only a superficial secret that could be found out with just a bit of research.

Namely, that secret was ‘They’re all important people who are working together to destroy the organization, and also conspired together to entrap August.’

So in other words, they had willingly painted targets on their back, and then decided to travel away from their home country to a more exposed place. They were pretty much begging to be assassinated.

The key point of the plan was to ensure someone would come after them. While dangerous, all of them had willingly participated in that mission, as they considered uncovering the organization more important than their personal safety.

“And that’s what everyone is busy with.”

Obviously, they were not just mere honeypots, as they were also surrounded with the means of capturing any assailants.

To be more specific, the Twelve Apostles were with them.

In total there were four of such officials, each of them protected by two of the Twelve Apostles, all of which were in disguise, hidden amongst the regular bodyguards of those officials.

That left four of the Twelve Apostles in Nirvana, three of which, including Esmeralda, were busy watching over the tournament, and the last one was Noin, protecting the Oracle.

The only female in those four was Esmeralda, who had to be present for the tournament, as people would constantly get badly injured, and the healing powers of her and the healer unit she commanded were necessitated all the time.

Doing all of that kept her too busy to be able to protect the Oracle as well.

“That seems like a reckless and dangerous path you’ve chosen to walk on…”

It was all a shocking revelation. That big tournament everyone was talking about all over the continent had been a lure for Ira Muerte all along.

Mira was still a bit taken aback by it all, but at least she fully understood why she was picked to be the new bodyguard.

Their enemy was an enormous organization, and while the Oracle was currently safe, there was no telling when someone exceedingly skilled would come for her. And when that happened, the Oracle’s bodyguard would need to be able to match that skill.

Noin would fit that role amongst those in Nirvana, except that he was impeded by the Oracle’s phobia against men, and the other Twelve Apostles were busy somewhere else.

That was when Mira came waltzing in. She had recently become famous as the Spirit Queen, and secretly she was one of the Nine Wisemen, who stood on equal footing with the Twelve Apostles.

On top of that, she also was a summoner, capable of raising an army if needed. It was almost like she was a godsend solution to all of Alma’s worries about the bodyguard.

“And also…”

There was something more Alma had done to make her lure more enticing. She had let it slip, on purpose, that the Oracle would go out undercover to watch the tournament as well.

That was the extent of things. Even the Oracle would become a lure.

“I planned all of that under the impression that Noin would be with her… Now I’ve been trying to cancel those arrangements, but it seems she was really looking forward to going out…”

With Noin at her side, the Oracle would have been safe enough to watch while munching on popcorn as a whole high level raid party attempted to take her. Sadly she could no longer get close to Noin, making that much harder.

To make things worse, Alma had already spread rumors about the Oracle’s planned outings, which Ira Muerte was sure to have intercepted, considering their information gathering abilities.

In other words, it would be impossible for her to go out and watch the fights unless she was under tight security. Hearing that had put her in rather low spirits.

“Hmm. Very well then, I’ll accept your request!”

Having heard the situation they were in, it did not take Mira much time to make up her mind.

She could easily assume that Ira Muerte would be hellbent on getting rid of the Oracle, who had put August in a chokehold that rendered his underground trading routes useless.

It was also evident that the Oracle was a brave girl, who chose to stand up against a powerful and evil organization that spanned across the continent. And more importantly, Mira wanted to cheer her up.

“Thank you, Grandpa!”  

“Thanks, Mirako. We really appreciate it.”

Everything would have gone smoothly if Noin could still do it, but that possibility had been ruined in an unexpected way. Now that Mira had stepped in, it was like a heavy weight had been lifted off Alma and Esmeralda’s shoulders as they thanked her.

“But are you sure your plan will work out?”

Mira understood why they needed her help to guard the Oracle, but she was still a bit skeptical about the whole plan of using various lures to obtain more information about Ira Muerte, which Alma made sound easy.

“I’m sure you know that there’s plenty of people out there who will do anything in exchange for money. What if they employ such people to do everything, and once we catch them they turn out to not know anything about the organization itself?”

Nirvana’s power was well known, so Ira Muerte was certain to send the best assassins at their disposal.

Except that there was no guarantee that those assassins would also know about the inner workings of Ira Muerte. The whole plan would fall apart if they turned out to be hired hands without much information.

“Well, that’s just a fifty-fifty gamble we’ll have to take.”

For some reason, Alma looked rather confident even as she declared it was a fifty-fifty, and Esmeralda expanded on it as she said, “I guess it’s time we talk about the fourth head of Ira Muerte then.”

The fourth head of the organization, in charge of the information gathering and assassinations team.

“Ah, that reminds me. You know that Jorg man you captured, Grandpa? According to our information, he’s also part of that team, and thanks to you, we’ve got their base intact and all of his men too. You really made things easy for us, Grandpa.”  

“Heh, that was no sweat off my back.”

Jorg, the boss of the assassin group Mira had found, was also involved with the fourth team of Ira Muerte, and Alma was certain that he would provide vital information once they interrogated him.

“On top of that, Ira Muerte tends to be really secretive all the time, so they hardly ever hire any outside help…”

The fourth team handled all things relating to information, and as some say, knowledge can be more valuable than money. They attempted to control the flow of information to their advantage, sometimes twisting the truth, and other times covering up certain incidents. Most of the organization’s top skilled members were in that team too.

It was also that team that would move whenever something important happened, especially if they wanted to keep things under wraps.

“It wouldn’t be an exaggeration to say this is the worst state the organization has ever been in, so I’d wager they’ll send their own best men to deal with us.”

There was no denying that one of their four heads was compromised due to the powers of the Oracle. And it was also true that they would never want anyone in their same line of work to catch wind of that.

Ira Muerte had stood at the top of such underground organizations for a long time, having a lot of authority in many fields. That was also the reason why many other criminals trusted them, which inflated their ego, and put them in a position where they could never allow others to see their weaknesses.

What had happened with August could easily shatter all the trust and respect they had built up.

There was nothing more embarrassing for Ira Muerte than having everyone else finding out that a young girl they only knew as the Oracle had made them lose five hundred billion Rils while also shutting down their underground trade routes.

The only way they had of getting out of that situation without word getting out was to deal with it internally with their own members, specifically those in higher ranks that knew about August’s plight. Or at least that was Alma’s hope.

“Hmmm, that sounded really complicated, but I guess they’ll just want to keep their shame to themselves.”

There was always the possibility that the Oracle would also reveal all the organization’s dirty and shameful secrets to a hypothetical mercenary that went after her, so the safest option would always be to send a high ranking member that was already aware of everything there was to know.

“That’s basically it. And their high positions also make them priority targets for us, since they’re the ones hiding and manipulating all the information involving the organization.”

That team was in charge of silencing any news that could be detrimental to the organization, just like what happened to August. And that was also why they knew the most secrets.

Alma had come up with the idea of organizing the whole tournament with the sole goal of capturing the people leading that team.

“How do I put this…it sounds like a really reckless and uncertain strategy.”

Mira expressed her unfiltered opinion.

She could see how it had a chance of working, but there was no guarantee that someone in a high position in that team would actually come. And while having the Oracle leave the palace to watch the tournament presented a good opportunity for an assassination, they could choose not to take the bait and find a way to infiltrate the palace regardless.

With all those uncertain factors, Mira was still a bit unconvinced, but Alma continued saying, “But actually, I think our chances of success have improved with you here, Grandpa.”

“And what’s that supposed to mean?”

Alma’s confidence was unwavering, and Mira wanted to know why. The answer turned out to be connected to Noin.

“Noin’s unbreakable defense is well known even outside of Nirvana, so they would be really careful knowing he’s guarding the Oracle. That’s what made me question whether they would actually attempt anything against her. But the important thing is that now I can assign Noin to stay in position somewhere else, thanks to you.”

Now that Noin had been relieved of his bodyguard duties, Alma was planning on making him show up publicly during the tournament, making the lure more enticing.

As the more he was seen outside, the more obvious it would become that the Oracle was no longer being guarded by him.

Alma believed it was safe to assume that Ira Muerte was aware of the Oracle’s phobia, thanks to the way her powers connected her to August. But in the end, it would not matter if they knew the real reason for the change of bodyguards. As long as it was someone else, the organization would see that as a chance to attack.

“The Oracle’s defense will have weakened, and they might as well attribute that to August’s wicked acts. So it makes sense that they’ll try to exploit that opening, right?”

Alma sounded fully confident of her plan, and she had a point. The logical conclusion was that August’s meddling had successfully weakened the Oracle’s perfect defense, replacing it with whatever was at hand for Alma.

“That’s true.”

Even if another of the Twelve Apostles had taken Noin’s place, their defensive abilities would be inferior. That was something Mira could agree with.

“And on top of it all, we could use her powers to let them know that the new bodyguard is you, Grandpa, or rather, the Spirit Queen. That could also help us, as you’ve become a pretty popular adventurer recently.”

The stories about Mira made her seem like a good fit to be a bodyguard, and her appearance would not trigger the Oracle’s phobia. Overall, Alma was convinced that Ira Muerte would not suspect anything, and simply assume that Mira was the first available person who fit the criteria necessary.

There was still the possibility of keeping Mira in disguise as some mysterious bodyguard, but Alma insisted that it would be easier for Ira Muerte to underestimate the Spirit Queen, a known summoner.

“No matter what the stories about you say, the people see the Spirit Queen as an up and coming adventurer. If anything, this will make them want to attack even more, not knowing that they’re rushing straight into the jaws of one of the Nine Wisemen who stands on equal footing as Noin. It’s the perfect strategy, wouldn’t you say?”

Alma looked really smug about the plan she had concocted, and Mira was starting to get convinced too, as she grinned and said, “That sounds like fun, let’s do it.”

Overall, that plan reminded Mira of those prank shows of world class professionals going undercover as amateurs to shock others, which made Mira’s motivation skyrocket.

“I know, it’s so exciting. I knew you’d also want to be part of this, Grandpa!”

While Mira always loved a good fight, back during the game days she would often be relegated to defensive duty.

The main reason for that were her Holy Knights, which excelled at defending, and could be given orders to automatically engage enemies they spotted even if the summoner had not seen them. On top of that, they were easy to summon in large numbers to rapidly enhance one’s defenses.

So overall, Mira was rather confident in her own abilities as bodyguard. But there was another reason that made her smirk with anticipation.

(This could be the perfect opportunity to test out my new ideas.)

She was thinking back to the month or so of free time she had at the Tower, during which she immersed herself in her research and experiments, some of which she believed could come in handy here. But she tried to keep those ideas secret for now, as she simply declared, “No one will touch even a hair of her as long as I’m her bodyguard.”

Hearing Mira’s confident words, Alma and Esmeralda thanked her one more time.

+++

# 320: The cost of research

“Just keep in mind that I still have a mission to complete before I can take over as bodyguard. Is that alright?” After agreeing to watch over the Oracle, Mira blurted that out.

She had been moved by the Oracle’s young determination and agreed to help, but she did not forget that her main mission was to find Meilin, a mission she had to complete before taking up a new one.

“Ah, I almost forgot! What do you need to do?! I’ll help with anything I can!”

Alma looked really thankful that Mira had agreed to be the Oracle’s bodyguard, and declared that without hesitation. Esmeralda followed soon after, saying, “Me too, I’ll help if there’s anything I can do.”

“Ohh, I’m glad to hear that. In that case, there’s actually something I’d like to ask…”

In reality, those words were exactly what Mira wanted to hear from them, so she pounced on the opportunity, replying, “Then could you show me the entry forms from the tournament participants?”

“You want the entry forms?”

That response was not exactly something Alma had been expecting, as she could only wonder what Mira wanted to find in those forms, and her eyes were starting to fill with curiosity.

“If that’s all Mirako wants, then I guess we can let her, right?” Esmeralda did not mind giving Mira access to those forms, but just like Alma, was intrigued by the reason behind that request.

“There’s a few thousands of registered participants already. Are you sure you want to look through that? It could take a lot of time…unless you want us to check with you?”

Esmeralda offered to assist her further, mainly driven by her curiosity, as she was essentially asking Mira to reveal what she was looking for so they could help as well.

“Yup yup, we’ll help with anything!”

Alma was also on board with that. Their insistence was slightly overbearing for Mira, but she also understood that she would need help to check the forms.

“I’ll have to take you up on that offer then.”

Mira replied to them, continuing, “I’m actually…” and explained the reason why she was in Nirvana in the first place. It did not take long to tell them her mission this time, as they already knew about her search for the Nine Wisemen.

Simply saying she was tracking down Grasping Meilin, one of the Nine Wisemen, was enough for them to connect the pieces.

“Oh, did Mei come too then?! Ah, actually, she probably did. Everyone has heard about this tournament by now.”

Surely enough, Esmeralda instantly figured things out. It was a surprising realization, but a bit of thinking made it obvious. Either way, she was happy to hear that, as the Nine Wisemen and the Twelve Apostles had an oddly tight friendship, which manifested especially strongly between Meilin and Esmeralda.

“I see, I see… Someone like Meilin would definitely come here, you’re right. Okay, I’ll arrange for it right away!”

Even the reason why Mira wanted the entry forms was obvious to Alma and Esmeralda now. So Alma agreed to get the forms ready for search within the night, so that they could work on the search the next morning.

That also concluded their discussion about missions and bodyguards, so their conversation devolved into a chat between girls(?) as they enjoyed the rest of their tea.

Overall it was a pleasant time, as they talked about the game times, what they had done ever since arriving to this world, and various funny and weird stories.

“I’m still blown away by the scale of this tournament of yours. Just how much did all of this cost to organize?”

Mira suddenly began to wonder about that.

She had heard that the winner prize for the free for all tournament bracket was five billion Rils, which was already an outlandish sum, but there was also a wealth of legendary weapons and other rewards. On top of that, the enormous venue and all the surrounding attractions which made it look almost like an amusement park also had to have cost a considerable amount.

A country like Arkite would never be able to afford organizing something like that, so Mira was naturally curious to know how much it had cost to prepare such a big event.

In response, Alma began to grin before casually saying, “Around two trillion.”

“Two tri…trillion..?”

That was a number with a dozen zeroes behind it, so large that no mere person would ever see something like that. Not even a large country would mobilize such quantities without heavy consideration.

Arkite’s entire national budget was a similar sum, and here it was being spent on a single event.

(I guess the rank two player country really is on a whole different level…)

If a smaller country like Arkite ever tried to organize such an event, it would be the last party before the country would run into the ground.

“I’ve gotta hand it to Nirvana. Not every country would be able to casually dump that kind of money for a single event…”

Mira replied that, still baffled by how different the two countries were. And while Alma remained smug about it, Esmeralda just stared at Alma in disbelief.

“Alma, really? There’s nothing to be proud about. Now listen here, Mirako, we might be a bigger country, but we don’t just have that kind of money sitting around. We were only barely afforded all of this after piling up all of our personal savings.”

Alma let out an awkward groan when Esmeralda revealed the truth.

Esmeralda continued explaining what had happened. The festival had only been theorized for some time, but some time into the current year, they were forced to accelerate things and put it into action.

The reason for that was a change in Ira Muerte.

They noticed that the organization had been suddenly weakened from a different source to the Oracle, and they had to put the tournament plan into motion to take advantage of that.

But that had happened after the national budget for the year had been decided, and there were not enough funds left to deploy that plan with such short notice. So on top of having to go over budget, all Twelve Apostles also had to empty their savings.

Which happened to be savings they had kept since back in the game. All spent in a matter of months.

In the end, a whole trillion came from the Twelve Apostles, which meant more than eighty billion Rils came from each one. Even that was a sum Mira could not imagine having herself.

“I can’t believe you were just hoarding that kind of money for so long… I don’t even have one percent of that to my name.”

It was not just the country, now Mira was also shocked by the wallets of the Twelve Apostles.

The Nine Wisemen and the Twelve Apostles were roughly equal in power, and had been active for roughly the same amount of time in the game days. And yet they were able to gather all that money, while Mira felt like just a single billion was more than she could ask for.

“I guess working in a different country really makes a difference…”

That discrepancy was a mystery for Mira. Even when she thought about it more, she felt like the wages in both countries were comparable. And then she noticed Alma and Esmeralda’s sharp stares at her.

“You can see it that way if you like. I mean, everyone over in Arkite is constantly wasting all their money on experiments and whatnot.”  

“It’s not as much the country as your habits. We’re always watching our budget to be responsible, but you guys over there…”

Saying that, Alma and Esmeralda heaved a collective sigh. They could not believe Mira’s audacity to complain about having no money when she was constantly spending all the money that passed through her hands.

“Ah…I mean, I don’t think that’s fair, I’ve never…never…hmm….hnngngngn…”

It was true that she spent money on experiments, some of which could be rather expensive. But even that should not be enough to create such an exponential rift between their collective wealth.

At first, Mira tried to protest that it still did not add up, until she thought about it, and a bit more, various events slowly resurfacing in her mind, and making her voice sound less certain.

(How much did that temple we built cost again…)

There were many holy abilities that could only be gained by praying in sanctified ground, or touching divine relics

And then one of the Wisemen came up with the idea of building a new temple, creating a new sanctified ground to see what new abilities they would gain.

The result of that was the cathedral district to the west of Lunatic Lake. There was a large cathedral dedicated to the Three Gods there, as well as the monasteries for various ascetics who wanted to live there.

As far as Mira could remember, building all of that had cost at the very least a hundred billion Rils, and their experiment had still not borne fruit, as it took a long time for a place to be recognized as sanctified ground.

(This reminds me, she also spent a crazy amount on that experiment…)

There were also magic spells that could be gained by burning various items as catalysts. Essentially powerful items contained a certain essence of power which could be distilled through flames, and sometimes they would combine like pieces of a puzzle to coalesce into a new magic spell.

But just like with puzzles, it was impossible to know which essences could fit together without knowing their ‘shape’ first. Luminaria had gotten obsessed with that method before, gathering all the items and weapons she could afford, only to burn all of them. It did not matter if they were rare, heroic, or even legendary weapons, they all were turned to ashes.

(Legendary weapons in particular go for a few billion in the market, so I guess saving up was never an option.)

In the end, Luminaria was able to gain only around five new spells, and the knowledge that collecting spells that way was not as easy as it seemed at first.

(I think Soul Howl was also collecting relics of the dead or something like that…)

It was common for historic characters known for being heroes or blessed by divine power to also possess items with special powers, often loved by their owners, and buried alongside them, which altered that power in different ways.

Necromancers were able to imbue their abilities with those additional powers.

In their eyes, those relics were not weapons of legends, but a way to add buffs like extra physical damage to necromancy spells.

That put Soul Howl on the hunt for relics left behind by heroes and holy men, as well as items left behind by the rare villains that managed to leave their name in history, genius academics, and even famous artists. It was easy to see how collecting such items could get expensive as well.

(Oh right, I may have spent a lot on that too…)

As more memories resurfaced, she also began to realize how much she had spent at various points in her past.

One big case was when she attempted to restore a ravaged sanctuary.

It was located northeast of Arkite, right in the middle of a mountain range. In the distant past, that place had been known as a paradise of abundant peace, inhabited by many sacred beasts.

But the whole place had burned down during a great war in the past, leaving the place barren.

Mira had decided to take up the task of restoring that place to its former glory. She employed various mysterious remedies to let the vegetation regrow, and erected a protective barrier around the area so it would not be burned again if war broke out.

Her efforts had been fruitful, as the place was once again functioning as a sanctuary, with some sacred and spectral beasts starting to gather there. And obviously enough, Mira, or Danbulf at the time, often went to visit that place to form as many Summoning Contracts as possible.

There were various other ravaged sanctuaries like that which she had worked on restoring, and with all the costs combined, that was also incredibly expensive.

Then there were the other expenses involving the Silver Linked Towers, like expanding the basement to have more space to conduct experiments, vast and complicated water control systems to carefully grow plants they needed for experiments, and so on. The longer Mira thought about it all, the more she realized how much the costs were piling up.

The stark difference between those living within strict budgets, and those spending blindly on whatever they wanted was becoming obvious.

“My current self only exists because of past sacrifices, mhm, mhm…”

In the end, Mira chose to simply wave off all of those expenses together with other past experiences, conveniently ignoring the truth. But Alma and Esmeralda continued staring at her with disapproval.

+++

# 321: Checking forms

After arriving at Ratnatraya, Mira was able to meet with Alma and Esmeralda for a late dinner, after which they took a bath, in separate bathrooms obviously, and Mira was given a guest room where she promptly fell asleep.

The next morning, Mira woke up, took care of her usual business, and then left the room feeling refreshed.

“Woah?!”

Mira flinched and took a step back upon noticing a maid quietly standing next to the door. A maid in a palace was something that gave her flashbacks of her nemesis, Lily.

“Good morning, Lady Mira. I’ll show you to breakfast if you’re ready to go.”

The maid spoke with a polite and calm voice, which was not too different from how Lily spoke as well, except that this maid did not have the same looming darkness to her that Mira dreaded so much, instead looking almost resplendent.

“I’m ready, let’s go.”

Somehow, Mira’s preconception of maids being the same as Lily had been burned strong into her mind, but in reality, such maids were the exception rather than the norm.

Either way, Mira realized she could keep her guard down in this palace, so she happily followed after the maid to breakfast.

“I may have overdone it a bit, eating so much early in the day.”

Mira muttered to herself after breakfast, which had been a buffet style meal. That was usually how the palace servants ate, while guests would be served carefully crafted course meals.

But Alma knew that Mira would prefer picking her own food instead of eating like nobles usually did. That decision had been perfect, as nothing could make Mira happier than being able to eat as much as she wanted of anything she wanted, which were mostly desserts.

When she was done eating, she followed the maid again and went to Alma’s room.

“Have a pleasant day.” The maid said before turning around to leave, and Mira thanked her for leading the way there.

“Good morning, Grandpa.”  

“Mm, good morning.”

After a brief greeting, Mira noticed the pile of documents on Alma’s desk, realizing that she also had a lot on her plate as empress.

Then Alma asked how Mira had slept, if she liked her breakfast, all the things they had learned thanks to Mira’s help the day before, about watching over the Oracle, and so on.

“Good morning, Mirako.”  

“Oh…good morning.”

Some time later, Esmeralda arrived as well, smiling radiantly as the tournament participation forms were ready for Mira to check them, just as promised the night before. Everything was gathered in a different room.

“I’ll go help too if I get some free time!”

As Mira and Esmeralda headed there, Alma saw them off with those words, and Mira hoped that it would happen soon.

Esmeralda took Mira to a large room filled with bookshelves, which she called the information bureau’s storage room.

It seemed to be at least three hundred meters long, and it was also incredibly tall, with four open levels stacked on top of each other visible from the entrance. That also went to show how much larger Nirvana was compared to Arkite, seeing how much space was needed to store all of the information gathered from across the country.

“Now this is another impressive place…”  

“Every time I come here I can feel my sense of reality warping too.”

After Mira muttered her first impression, Esmeralda also concurred with an awkward voice. Esmeralda had lived most of her life amongst the common people, so sometimes she was also overwhelmed by life in the palace.

They walked across the room, into a separate one that was mostly used to review documents before storing them in the main shelves.

“There’s…so much stuff.”

There were many tables and chairs in that room, and Mira quickly spotted a tall pile of documents on a large table in a corner, just the sight of which made her feel exhausted. That was the pile with all of the tournament participation forms.

“Alright Mirako, I also have some work to do first before I can help…so good luck.”

Esmeralda had only been there to show Mira the way, and now had to go back to work.

Alma and Esmeralda had offered to help before, but as one was the empress and the other one of the Twelve Apostles, they had other important duties to take care of first.

“Well, I should be thankful that they took the time to organize it like this in the first place…”

She felt slightly abandoned, but with no time to waste, she reached for the first bundle of files.

The forms had been separated by the different tournament brackets, some being purely for spellcasters, or for warriors younger than eighty years old.

The forms themselves were organized by the time they were registered, so the earliest submissions came first.

Knowing Meilin’s personality, she was sure to register for the free-for-all tournament. And when accounting for the scale of the event, she would have rushed to register as soon as possible, so her form should be near the top.

“Now, let’s just hope I can find her…”

Wishing for things to go well, Mira began looking through the free-for-all forms.

It really struck her how convenient digital databases were, as one could simply input a few conditions and she would get everything sorted the way she wanted.

Simply being able to view all applications with Sage as the participant’s class would have made things a lot easier. As she continued thinking about such things, she went through the forms one after another, for more than half an hour.

“Ah…she actually did it.”

She had found a form with Martial Sage as the class. That was a term Meilin had come up with and gotten attached to, mostly known amongst their friend group. It signified her pride as a martial artist, as well as a sage.

Then she checked the name, which turned out to be Meimei.

The Sage Wiseman was called Meilin, which was a rather well known name. So it made sense that she was using a fake name, but knowing her, it seemed obvious that she would come up with such a similar name as well.

“Who would’ve thought that I’d be able to read her like this. Hmm… Maybe I’ve unlocked my abilities as a detective after my search for Fuzzy Dice!”

Mira grinned with satisfaction. She was convinced that this Meimei was actually Meilin. At the same time, she was a bit surprised by how quickly she had found it, considering the tall pile of forms nearby. She almost felt bad for everyone who had worked to bring them there, only for her to barely look through a fraction of them.

“Well, maybe I should just say I got lucky…”

As she thought of ways to explain it, she heard approaching footsteps and then the door opening.

“Grandpa, we’ve come to help!”  

“How’s your search going?”

Alma and Esmeralda showed up. They had finished their official duties as fast as possible to come help, just like they had promised.

“Ohh, thank you for coming all the way here, though…”

It no longer was necessary, as she had already found it. Instead of saying with words, she just held up the form.

“What happened?”

The two did not know what to make out of that, so they moved closer to check the form, and a short time later they exclaimed, “Ah…” at the same time.

“This has to be Meilin, right?”  

“Yes, I’m sure it’s her.”

Both of them were also convinced that it had to be Meilin’s form. It was a weird feeling seeing that when they had come with every intention to dig through the mountain of forms, but they just laughed together realizing it had been done.

“Okay, and let’s see where she’s staying…”

Meilin had come to the tournament as they had expected. That was something Mira had been certain of before, and now came the next step, finding out the exact place she was staying at.

Part of the registration process involved writing down the name of the inn one was staying at, or the tent number of the provisionary camp. That piece of information would be a great help in finding the location of Meilin, who was always traveling around to train and improve her skills.

“It says…Adams Residence, where’s that?”  

“Oh huh, where could that be?”

There was nothing there other than Adams Residence. They checked a register of all inns in Ratnatraya just in case, but there was no place called that. Which could only mean one thing.

“So this means she’s staying at some private residence…”  

“Probably, yes.”  

“I don’t know what else this could mean.”

All three were in agreement of that. Meilin was staying with someone related to the name Adams.

“Adams…who could that be?”

An inn would have been much easier to track down than a private residence. Which was made even more difficult by the fact that Adams was not an uncommon name, and Ratnatraya was a large city with hundreds of thousands of residents. There were way too many possibilities.

“I guess going to public records and getting a list of everyone called Adams could be an option.”

With no other leads, their only recourse would be to go knock on the doors of anyone named Adams. Public records would have a registry of the city residents, so Alma suggested going there, but Mira did not look thrilled about it.

“I still can’t believe that she’s actually staying with someone. I wonder if they’re friends or something?”

Esmeralda mumbled in thought. It was not easy to imagine a wandering sage like Meilin to have a good enough friend to stay with.

“Ah, Meilin can be pretty cute when she’s keeping still, so maybe…” Alma then muttered that out of nowhere, which alluded to a not very wholesome possibility.

“Yeah no, I don’t think we should worry about that.”

Esmeralda quickly shot down the idea. No matter what situation Meilin was in, she was not the type of girl who could be coerced into such things. But that made a different possibility appear in their minds. There were plenty of other less forceful and more deceitful ways around it.

“Adams, huh…”  

“Yes, some Adams…”  

“Well, at least we have a lead. We’ll just have to investigate whoever this Adams is.”

There was little to gain by continuing to talk about it here, so Mira wanted to head to public records already.

“Umm, I just brought the latest forms, should I leave them here as well?”

Before Mira could say anything, a woman knocked on the door and looked inside.  

She was the person Esmeralda had appointed to bring in all the forms that were piled up on the table. Those orders simply mentioned all of them, so she was under the impression that all the new forms that had just been submitted also needed to be carried there.

“Thank you, but you can put those back.”

They had found someone who was likely Meilin already, so there was no need for more forms. Esmeralda thanked that woman for her work and sent her back, who bowed saying, “I understand.”

But she did not turn around to leave. Instead she stood there nervously, her gaze downcast as she thought hard about something.

“Is there anything else?”

When Esmeralda asked that, the woman seemed to make up her mind as she raised her face.

“Umm… Did Sir Adams do something wrong?!” She asked, looking more anxious than worried. Apparently she had managed to overhear them talking about Adams moments before she entered the room.

And she seemed to know someone by the name of Adams as well, so it made sense for her mind to come up with all sorts of reasons why the empress and one of the Twelve Apostles was talking about him.

“Oh…would you mind telling us more about this Sir Adams?”

There just so happened to be an Adams so close by. It could just be a coincidence, but Mira had a hunch that there was more to it, and was the first one to react by asking that.

“Umm…I just…”

The woman knew the empress Alma and the Apostle Esmeralda, but had no idea who the unknown girl with them was. Still, Mira spoke so directly with an imposing attitude that the woman instinctively replied.

Sir Adams was the leader of a knight unit, and had been appointed to stand watch by the tournament registration front desk.

“Ohh…the front desk…”

Those words alone gave Mira an idea, as well as hope that things would end up taking less effort than she thought.

Knowing Meilin, she probably went to enter the tournament straight away, without even thinking about stopping by at an inn, which would lead to various issues when filling out that spot in the form.

“Tell me, how would you describe this Sir Adams’ personality? For example, do you think he would pick up and take care of a lone stray kitty?”

Mira decided to pry deeper, which made the woman hesitate a bit, beginning to blush as she finally replied.

“Yes, I think he would. I’ve seen him bring in injured strays in the past. He’s also really responsible, kind to everyone, but is also strong and always steps in to stop rowdy people before they start fights.”

Adams appeared to be a really good person, which was maybe why the woman felt compelled to interrupt a conversation between Alma and Esmeralda.

“Hmmm, I think I see what’s going on now…”  

“Oh my, now this is unexpected.”

Alma and Esmeralda had also taken notice of certain feelings harbored by that woman, making them grin teasingly, but not maliciously.

Mira also noticed that, but she just said, “Interesting,” while narrowing her gaze.

But the woman assumed that they were not convinced by her response yet, and as she still did not know why they were talking about Adams, she felt the need to bring up a more recent example, all to clear his name of any suspicion.

“Umm… Actually…there was this time, just a month ago. There was this young girl who came to enter the tournament…”

The story the woman told was exactly what Mira had been picturing already.

When that girl came to register, she had initially filled out her staying place as “Anywhere.” That did not really make much sense, so the receptionist asked her to clarify what she meant, and the girl said that she would stay at a nearby forest, or a park, or out in the streets, so simply anywhere.

Everyone behind the desk became concerned hearing that. While they trusted the guards would keep the streets relatively safe, they did not want to imagine a girl camping out alone like that.

But the girl’s finances were not good enough for her to stay in an inn. For a moment, she considered staying in the housing provided by the tournament for participants, but quickly rejected it when she heard that there was a set schedule when meals would be served, and a curfew.

(That does sound like her a lot. She always only wanted to eat what she wanted, and sleep whenever she saw fit.)

There was still no confirmation that the girl in the story was actually Meilin, but Mira was growing increasingly convinced of it as she listened to the woman.

In the end, the girl insisted that she would stay anywhere, but those behind the desk kept worrying and wanted to convince her to use the facilities offered by the tournament. The discussion was going nowhere, until Adams arrived after hearing of the situation.

“Sir Adams agreed that Anywhere was not a suitable response for the form, and so he came up with another solution.”

She continued talking passionately and with conviction.

The girl had no money for inns, but was too free-spirited to fit in with the rest. Faced with that, Adams decided to invite her to stay at his house. Now that girl was happily staying there, and was getting along with everyone else living there as well, something the woman said with a tinge of jealousy in her voice.

“That explains everything.”  

“I guess things are going well then.”  

“Yes, he’s a really good person.”

Everything the woman had just said lined up perfectly with the details listed in Meimei’s form.

Mira and the other two also connected the dots and nodded satisfied with the story. The woman saw that reaction and her face lit up with relief.

(Things are looking very promising now!)

Mira was excited that her search for the Adams Residence had been made so much shorter. All she needed to do now was go visit the house of Sir Adams, and talk to Meimei, who was most definitely Meilin.

“Alright, then I’ll have Adams come here to talk about it.”

Alma said that, wanting to move things forward. That immediately made the woman stiffen up again.

It was normal to be worried knowing that the person one was attracted to was being summoned by the empress, and Esmeralda noticed that change in the woman, so she smiled kindly and reassured her, “Don’t worry, he didn’t do anything bad.”

“I understand, I’ll let him know right away.”

Esmeralda had managed to dispel her worries, so the woman quickly knelt and bowed before running off to find Adams.

While they waited, and since they were already within the archives of the palace, they began to look through Adams’ files to learn more about him.

They wanted to know what kind of person was looking over the girl they believed was Meilin, and they were also curious about the man who had smitten the heart of the woman from earlier.

They really just were being nosy for the sake of it.

++++

# Not Sure, Another World - Chapter 157 -  The World is much smaller than I thought

So we met up with Arisa and Kuro as they were returning from the forest, and we decided to speak with the Village Chief…

“No, no, pardon me. I didn’t mean to cause you such trouble…”  

“Aah, no no! Don’t worry about it!”  

“I’ve already submitted a petition to the Lord through the Magistrate, and they said they’d be able to assist… Please forgive us for—”  

“No no, it’s all okay! That is, Mina looked like she was about to cry, so we decided to at least listen to what she had to say! That is… if we take on requests directly like this… it often leads to arguments…”  

“Ah… Well, that’s right… It would be troublesome for us as well if that were to happen…”  

“Is, is that so? Haha…”

Yeah, it seems like this problem was already being addressed. Both Lily and the Village Chief both exchanged awkward glances with each other, the former not wanting to accept the requests in order to avoid trouble, and the latter not wanting us to accept the request. Now we just need to do something about this awkward atmosphere.

“Well, that’s that… Mina! Seriously, you’re doing something unnecessary!”  

“But~…”  

“No buts! There, move along!”  

“Yes…”  

“Haa… Honestly, this child is such trouble.”

“No no, that’s just how worried she is about her mother, so please don’t be angry.”  

“I appreciate you saying that… But, that’s right… As I said before, the issue with the monster has already been dealt with, how about talking with the Magistrate? It may cause problems if we were to hire you, but perhaps the Magistrate may have an idea? I’m probably not the one to say this, but having more fighting power couldn’t hurt…”  

“Eh? Ah, no… Can we huddle for a moment? … Yes, then… Ren, Arisa, what should we do?”
